Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the uterine solution comes from coldness and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are relaxed, and cannot be cured by methods of cures; and you see the patient suffering strongly and having great virtue, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said here before or the stomach cautery, at the circulatory cautery; and three subtlety cauteries around the belly, each as fine as a clavicle, and two cauteres on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the thumb, and one cautery on each kneecap, and two small cauteres on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemroids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and are caused by gross cold and moist humors corrupted, and are not cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind the almacate pouch and gradually forming a triangle, and one cautery below the belly. Two should be done;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face swelling, then one must make a great cautery on the stomach, as said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mucus everywhere at all the cauterizing; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fatness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut to the fatness which is called "thelul", if you scrape off the cautery that appears as a razor, and then put it all ablaze on that fatness being cut; and leave your hand so long until the cauterizers come out at the birth of the vein, from which blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much fatness, then cauterize each one just as we have said; after curing with ointments for as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize a great cautery on the navel, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an uncured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When to anyone comes a fistula, and it is inflamed and discharges putridity and corrupted moisture, then you must prove all of it with a subtle tent, and be sure that you know the depth of the tent entirely. Afterward, scrape off the cautery which appears as a razor, and fill it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and continue the cautery until those corrupted parts are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of what is needed; and beware not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, then be wary of these places, and do not make fires except in a charred place, and think that it is not yet healed; after curing the wound until it is healed, and if the wound is sauced, and the matters are removed long times, then know that the wound is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the wound is torn open, and corrupted bone to the front; and thus as one of those that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and from excessive moisture, and does not take shape like a woman's, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other at the cautery clavicle which we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizers in a line, and they will cause greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part behind the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, and one to the right and one to the left, and each cautery be as long as a thumb's breadth; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need them; and the cauterizers be clavicle-shaped according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not leave a means for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizers around the mouth, as we said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizers behind the back; and be the cauterizers clavicle-shaped, as we said.
de la hainche	of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the groin of the haunch, and because of this, it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the wound of departure is found, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the groin of the haunch with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the wound around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and let the cauterizers be such as those which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizers are not present, make three large cauterizers of the olivaire, and let them be as deep as all the colors; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin of the haunch, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is cured with what we have said in the division and the cure does not hold, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors by fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: namely, together medicines burning, and cauterization by fire. Cauterization by fire is according to many manners, one of which is this: you must make three triangular cauterizers on the groin of the haunch in this form, and make a good depth and size, and have between each cautery a space equal to the thickness of a thumb, and be the cauterizers olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the haunch, therefore there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that it should be cauterized at the cautery of the circle which we said before in the dislocation of the haunch; but make it in this manner so that the circle contains all the haunch and all the spaces of the color are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the haunch and does not reach as far as the thigh or knee. And if it comes as far as the thigh and knee, then make two cauterizers on either side where the patient says that the pain holds, and one cautery above the ankle three thumbs to the left part; and be the cauterizers cutellaire, and let the flesh of the color be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two toes or almost so, then cauterize where they feel the pain, either three points or four at the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more; and if it seems that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cautery at the cutellaire or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizers that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more great nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who had a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they were left so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all over the feet. After a purging of the belly in which he got his death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a fire cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be scalded until it is entirely red and gives off sweet smells, and then put on the boil of the sick person's backside, and be turned over on the healthy side; and have one fire cauterization repeated and leave it three days; and then make a poultice with butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure by anointing until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use a little of this cauterization due to the fear of its gaze, and if we see none who use it; and yet these are good cauterizations, which can be borne by those where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or from excessive evacuation or from similar cold matter spread out, none of these likenesses is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be freed from fetid pills or similar things, and one makes signs on the back where the pain stays, three lines marked with an "enche", and in each line five or more cauterizations depending on the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and make the cauterization according to the cauterization called "poins"; and if you see, do three or four cauterizations at the cauterizing point middle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight, thin skin when they rise, and fear; and you will find in the last vertebra of the back and on our appearance which appears above other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you know how to cure it, then cauterize at the cauterizing point of that according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	And so the cauterization will prick each part of the vertebra equally. And if you see, then cauterize around the vertebra at the piercing point 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be close to one another. After cure, leave it so long as it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not administer a cauterization in gibbosity which is in spasms of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is due to moistors that are spread out in each member of the body, and when pain comes into feet, which physicians properly call "podagre", and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, if the cauterization makes a point at every point; and if pains come to just above the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make three or four cauterizations on each part of the joint, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand back for as long as the sparks of fire are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to just above the knee and back, then administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the wrist 2 lines; and if there remains pain in the shoulders, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to just above the hips or just above the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance with the patient and take medicines. For if you do good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the itch of the scrofula
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch comes to pustules, and the boils descend to the groin and it is new, then it is necessary that when you see it cured, he does not annoy me that day; and that he uses things which loosen his bowels, so that the evil descends from his belly; after make him sit on his back between my hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boils are healed, and then cauterize below the itch on the bone of the elbow, and mark a sign like a half-circle above the body; then scald the cauterization in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	so that it is white and gives off sweet smells. Then reset the boils to their place; and make him hold his hand on it so they do not return backwards; and work well the hips on the patient, and put a cushion and a servant under them on the hips, and another one on the chest which holds his hands; then put the cauterization on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again another time until you reach the bone; and be mindful subtly that the boil does not burst when you make the cauterization; nor burn him; and that by this the patient may not die or suffer other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cauterization, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauterizations of children be subtle according to their measure, and those of big people also big according to theirs; after three days cure the place of the cauterization with butter until the scarring is removed; after treat him with other ointments until he is healed, and make the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that their swellings be made to subside slowly, so that the boil does not burst when they will go into chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, give him a well-made bandage and apply it for another 40 days; and have good rest, so that he does not overwork himself and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he has followed this instruction, he is entirely healed. And I will say afterwards about the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the itch of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When itches come to other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make one cauterization of the same cauterization repeated according to its quantity, and let the third part of fire be burned; after cure according to what we have said; and some of the old ones have said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but mark the first sign on the edge and make a line across the itch above and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cauterization like a hinge. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, whether it falls or is hurt, and that pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with the fire caustic called "points", and the cauteries should be made according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location of twists and pain. If he is healed from the first cauterization, that's good; if not, start another one on top of it, for these customs are such that the member must change where it is nearest, so you should make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The sick are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take heed if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not return or remain, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then do 5 cauteries on the head: 1 inside the head up to the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the hair; and 2 on each horn, and 1 behind on the back of the head; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of thick humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries we have said on the head, and 1 cauterization behind the nape of the neck, and 2 cauteries on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and 1 great one on the hump and another below, and 2 on each shoulder; and 2 on the sides, and 2 on the tendons of the breast, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take heed of the nerves that are behind the calcant, lest you burn them; and sometimes make a cauterization on the bone of the shoulder-blade, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I make of a cauterization, the more it brings aid and moves the profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron. Afterward, apply a poultice made with flour and honey and other cures until he is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, but it is not healed, then one makes cauteries on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and the cauteries should be a little way into the flesh of the vein. Then apply an ointment treatment until he is healed. And sometimes one makes a cauterization at the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; and yet no one interferes if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the issues of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulcers" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is worth nothing, then one cauterizes with a cauterization a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh of the vein, until the blenchour is removed, and its color changes; then apply a poultice made with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of colander and almond, each one in equal parts; and mix everything together, and tie it up with a cloth, and air it at the bedside until he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When syphilis comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, then cauterize around the chancre with a cauterization that seems like a circle, all around the tour of the chancre. And yet wise men say that one should make a cauterization also in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem to me good, for I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen once or twice; and it is a more rightful thing to cauterize around, with the cauterization that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it cannot be killed, either because of its superfluity or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries in succession; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization so that its form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the vein, and be such cauteries that the patient feels it outside in this way, so that the course of the purulence is alleviated. Afterward, apply a treatment until he is healed perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of sickness is called "corrodens", and it's nothing other than a wasting away of the member, for it wastes away members just like fire consumes dry leaves. If you see this disease in someone who can bear cauterization with fire together, then heat the cauteries very little and big, according to what's needed at the place where the sickness is; afterward, cauterize all over until you remove all the corruption, so that nothing remains of it, except for everything that's corrupted to be removed. And then leave it three days, and put on the heated cauteries that suffer burns with oil until the ashes of fire are removed, and all the corruption. Afterward, apply a treatment with ointments engendering flesh. If you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, it's good; but if not, then start again the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted flesh. And this wasting away has sometimes been cured by medicine in place of fire cauterization; but still, fire cauterization is more helpful, and I have already said the cure with medicine in the division: take as much as you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pins which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	A great many times it happens that at the feet a disease occurs which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large, festering thing that hurts the foot. And the treatment for this disease is done in two ways. It's to know that there are two manners of cautery. The one by fire, and the other by hot water. By fire it is that you make a cautery on the hair as if it were a vulture's feather, and it must be made of good iron to a measure that it can penetrate the nail from all sides, and have subtle edges; after which put everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it reaches the tip of the nail; and let it sit thus for three days until it begins to emit pus; then make an ointment with wild marjoram crushed with salt, and leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the foot with oil anointing it as long as it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted on the outside of the body, and many times it happens in hands and feet, then you must bring a hot water cautery; and it is done thus: take an earthen or iron rod, or a vulture's feather, and put it on the nail and the surrounding area, that is to say, pins and veins; and place the rod so that it surrounds everything, then put a little bit of hot water there, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water's way deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer a little the stinging of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself from all its roots. Do this after another, until you have reached all those on the body, then cure them with ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cures of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shiver from cold or heat, or quartan fever, or another, then you must make four cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the belly, and one above the stomach at the olive-shaped cauterization; if the patient shivers, and the healthiness of the cold disease will hasten.
des pustules puans	the stinking pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes pus-filled boils or stinking pimples appear on the body, which come from corrupted matter. Then it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization of myrtle wood, so that the point is seized by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cautery. And sometimes one does not cauterize them at first when they appear, according to this manner, and they do not grow any further forward, but are broken down the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times it happens that great flows of blood come from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tight until the blood is appeased beneath your fingers, and no more drips; then take a few small and large cauterizations, all red from fire, and take one, either great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put it on that vein which you are holding with your two fingers, and hold the cautery thus until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spouts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cauterization is extinguished, then take quickly another one of the cauterizations that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is staunched; and take care that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well staunched without one of the three ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong bandaging with thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and strained in a suitable manner.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the stanching by binding tightly with cloths or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if there is no benefit whatsoever.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein just as we have said, and stretch them well until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move his hand, but moisten with cold water often enough so that the blood is congealed, thickened, and staunched; and make inquiries ahead about what he needs in terms of cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in our first chapter all the diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the remedies and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from head to feet, and I will go on in this chapter by the same way for those who want to find things more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and therefore it is necessary to exercise greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness. For many kinds of people come to cures. Some come from such a state with their disease that they will die quickly because of the severity of their illness and the greatness of their harm; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these are those who will give you their senses and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful. It does not behoove you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of and can take and hold; and use pronouncement and indication in the cures of your diseases where salvation is converted; and this will help you to acquire good renown, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Here is the translation:
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in describing chapter by chapter, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have described from the beginning to the end, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Two full heads of water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often afflicts children at childbirth, and when the midwife constrains too tightly the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those that I have seen died quickly; and therefore it seems to me that it is best to hasten the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew bigger each day until it could no longer be sustained; and believed so much moisture that he would die, and this moisture is assembled below the bone above the forehead, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut a wide incision in the head's midst; and let it be as long as two inches, until the moisture runs out; and look at the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opening on each side, and the water jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and it does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture outside. Afterwards, close the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil in them, and let it be thus for five days; then loosen it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head drain equally, and then allow the patient to eat dry meat without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the great opening of the abscess appears, and the assembly of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then at the place where the abscess opens, and the filling of water, and make the incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if there comes a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease which is called "catarre" in the eyes or at the breast, and the disease is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help at all, then the final cure is the cautery with what one will cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them cut off, the patient should bend his head back; afterwards, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then extract the patient's neck to all one cloth; then look where the vein bites, and the marks of both are after the ears, and they are not responsive; then mark the marks with encaustic; then cut off one and the other with an acute spatula two parts as long as the incision comes up to the bone, and it should be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatula below the artery and cut above it, cutting just as two would crosswise.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will jump out continuously outside.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark with encaustic and cut up to the bone; and what needs to be done about the blood letting outside is .vi. c., and by chance a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the forehead, then cut off that which abscesses do not come from, then drain the wound and bind it, and apply ointment treatment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and sharp catarrh, because of the moisture of tears and heats in the temples and old forgotten and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and all that does not help at all, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his temples' hairs, and listens to the artery which appears in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and is not responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and rise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above with pincers, and separate well the webs that are below each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it to the point of the unguent, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two chits. For if it is not cut off, it will not flow at all outside.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood of .vi. c., up to .iii.; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that no purulence may come before the healing of the wound, and there be decorremens of blood; then cut off the superfluity which is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the remaining part with the cautery knife up to the bone until the arteries are cut off; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is help to finish the moistures: therefore it is of greater aid to the moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts a well-made tent on top; and when one removes them, be careful with dry medicines that bring forth flesh and tents until they are healed; and if there is no cort of the artery as long as you work, then hasten to cauterize by cautery, or take vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is staunched; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on top of the place until the blood congeals, and rise the place with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as necessary; and what is most important and lighter in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting into two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to keep their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thick, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two cutlery pieces a space of a good thumb's length, and then when you have signed to join the two parts, and you must put the hot iron on so that it reaches just to the bone, and make the incision in two places; and be distant between the two joints because this cautery is not done from top to bottom; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing down from the veins that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not benefit at all from the medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the patient growing red, and feeling the forehead to be agitated as if with fear; and the skin is tender and moist so that the hairs of the paper are fallen, and the papers are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they used to call it the "blunt cure" in olden times, and is that you do behind the patient who has this disease, by cutting off the hairs on their forehead; then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions should be as big as two fingers all the way down to the nose, and the other two as wide as two fingers at the temples above the papers, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are at the temples above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuity of the jawbones, and each wound should be the size of three fingerbreadths across the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to absorb the blood, then pour the spatula's liquid from two parts, and this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is next to the temple all the way down to the second incision; and scrape out all the kernel that is between the two cuts right up to the suture that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision all the way down to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first incision the instrument which is called "culterelle", and it is very sharp on one side, and soft on the other side, not at all sharp, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sharp edge towards the fatty part of the kernel, and the soft edge towards the bone, and insert it so that it comes to the middle incision. And cut all the vessels that flow down from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous right up to what opens from the kernel, and then make another incision in the middle incision right up to the other one; and then extract the blood equally, and express the bone for the blood taken; then put a patch of old cotton in each incision, and place moist cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and ass's milk on top, and take care that abscesses do not form; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great quantities of lukewarm water, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone comes with a severe catarrh as usual, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening the sight, and the papers burned; and the hairs falling, and the head in the forehead in great pain, and the patient is worn out; then learn through these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come forth except from many voices, and the mother cure that is there, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And is that you instruct the patient to cut their forehead, then make a large incision in the forehead and another one of about an inch long. Begin from the left temple to the right temple, and be the incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, let all the blood flow onto a sponge, and then dry between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen there; then bind with moist cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and take care not to form an abscess; when it is healed, you should rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then apply ointments that make flesh come.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of wheat flower and three parts of galenicals, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds to bring forth flesh all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of three things: either grains, or beasts, or pebbles from the mine or similar things like iron; or seed, such as jay's wheat, lentils, peas; or flowing things like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it comes out of the ear a pebble or other thing that does not belong to the ear and does not grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun. If you see a pebble, extract some small amount of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make the nostrils narrow when the symptoms come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear above. Many times it comes forth through this cure; and if it does not come forth, then administer extraction with subtle forceps, and this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps forth through the forceps, that's good; if not, then administer extraction with a subtle onyx file of small double reed; and if it does not jump forth through this, then make a ring of iron and insert the chief of the ring or ear plug firmly into the ear canal, and stop what is around the ring from entering with it using soft wax; then treat it further, for many times it comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this way, then take a lump of which takes birds and put some instrument that is pointed to do so, and wrap it with a small amount of cotton; then press the lump on the pebble or whatever it is, and treat further.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump forth through all these things that we have said, then you should hasten to cut the ear, lest an abscess form and spasms occur; and the manner of cutting is as follows: first, let the patient recover from the cephalic disease, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or bone depends; and be the incision like a moon, as long as you come to the pebble, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is swelling that has formed and it is inflamed, administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one quarter of a spoonful held subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision to that swelling. But do not do this when you think the swelling is moist because of the moisture in the ear, until you have divided it into many pieces; then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction, as we said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.
