Then the patient should use condimentous discharge first in the ear, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let it sit on that same ear where the liquid is. If it jumps forth because of this, it's good. If not, then take many stones according to their length, and make them hot by the fire; and put one or two pieces of the patient's ear into it, and lift up the other part from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this stone upon stone until all the liquid has come out, and thus it will jump forth entirely; and if you see, then take one reed, and put one of its ends in the ear, and the other end in the fire until the thicker part of the reed is burned; then do the rest of the rest with other reeds as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the beast, if it has a small body, like a mouse and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, administer an extraction with pincers; and it is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of earworms from the ears, when you have cured as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun: if you see any worms, treat them with subtle pincers; and if you do not see, take the cane where there is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle end of the cane in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly on the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, stop around the cane with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not jump forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the destruction of worms, and you will find it in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, according to the form which is there so you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be made of thick silver or bronze below to one small hole, and above over for distilling; and to press inside the distillation with one instrument of well-made bronze for this purpose, and if you see take one scraper and wrap it around the pointed part with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into it, and whatever medicines you have in the cane, and let the cane be in the ear; then blow inside the scraper to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled out of the ear; and if the patient feels inside, and the distillations are one pot heated by fire thus that it distills into the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicines would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppering of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in the ear; and this same thing happens to men by stoppering of wound or char born inside the ear, and these stoppings come sometimes quite far into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there is one pot too much for the perforation, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes quite far in, if one cannot see it, is from grievous inflammation in multiple dispositions, and that which one sees, needs you to put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see apparent opacity, then work with all this spoonful according to the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be gentle and cautious in front and back of the whole ear, so that it does not harm the ear; if the opacity is of born char or flesh of the ear, then take it with subtle pincers and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opacity is quite far in the ear, then take a subtle and light scraper and heat it slightly by fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the opacity which the patient feels grief at hearing, cut lightly, and beware that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and soak in Egyptian balm.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on vitriol broth; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and apply another moistened tent made of rosate oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is sound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes from the wound, then dip a sponge in cold water, and wrap it around the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paper-makers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This mixture that comes from paper-makers of eggs when they are moist and dry, needs you to stretch them with forceps and pincers, and cut off a spoonful of their roots; then put on the white vitriol broth.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the skin is peeled off, then cauterize the lenticular subtlety of the cautery, and the cauterizing after the incision works as a remedy; and many times they repair themselves, except that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	of the hawthorn
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come from papermakers of eggs certain things that resemble hawthorn in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the work is as follows: take heed if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it is a light thing to know; then cut out the width, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with pincers, and cut. If you cannot cut without piercing the paper slightly, do not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, assemble a seam, and cure until it is sound; and if it is small, make no force, for the ointments will soon restore it and bring forth flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et if the wax is dripping inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn it over and scrape off any impurities, and press it firmly from one side to the other; and if the paper is displaced by the incision, this does not matter; and when the wax is scraped off, then remove the salt water from the ear and cure the part of those who suffer from a wound as long as the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is formed in the membranes of the eyelids above, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they come to suffer from cataracts in the mornings, and they are unable to gaze at the sunlight because the tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces soon, and sleep above, and their membranes are wet beneath their eyelids, covered by the exinach that appears in the eye. And when you press the eye with your thumb and feel the exinach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient puts their head in your lap; and then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent-like shape around it, according to the quantity of exinach from each part, and put it on them; and press with your thumb on both sides so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle; then make an incision in the moist area above the spine, cutting a slit as wide as the wound one makes when opening a vein; and cut the skin so deeply that you come to the exinach; and in several positions, the exinach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take it out as one piece of cloth that has been folded between your thumbs at the edge, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to push it into the slit, lest you reach all the way to the oil, and you hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, then slightly widen the slit until it appears; then take it out as we have said, then wet the cloths with oil and water, and put them on the eye, and strain through bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who boil and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then he cures it until he is healed. And if it comes to a hot abscess, then he cures it with poultices soothing it until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the eyelids other than natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of illnesses such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albugine, until it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes; and there is a cure in three ways: either by fire cautery together, or by medicinal water according to what is written in the chapter on cautery, and this is done either by incision and suturing or by caustics, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid paper towards your left hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, then insert an awl into each thread above; and have this at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow from these hairs, and pull one thread upwards along the entire paper, and turn it to a razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, all the way to the spine, from the great tear duct down to the small one; then extract one thread, and put under the paper a small tent made of cotton and cloth, then sign on top of the paper a figure like that of myrtle, and although it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the eyelid paper being divided into.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is one who needs to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the eyelid paper is softened; then make all along the spine above the two lines you have marked, and start from the great tear duct down to the small one; and let it be one of the slits near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert an onyx into one of the two angles of the key, then skin it entirely; then assemble the two lips with a suture made of a fine wool thread, and stop the bleeding, and make the superfluous threads above the two eyelids stick to something, if you see fit; and if not, don't bother; then leave the suture and the threads for three days or four; then cure the wound without suture or constraining things, because the eyelid paper revives with the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is bitter (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaves of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three onyx stones unconnected according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above in small pieces evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and things are not equal, take an awl with one thread and insert it into the figure; then put another thread at the great tear duct and the second thread at the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your thumbs; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and at times it happens that the hairs of the eyelid paper are converted: then it is necessary to use what we have said about incision; but the suture in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of caustics is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make an incision in it according to what I have said, and then make two caustics by art, and two fine threads as long as the eyelid paper and the width of the spine are; and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of what rises from the eyelid paper, and strain the two caustics from the two parts in form; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and turn black and fall away, until it drops off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, then the wound will be more severe, and you should care for it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is lifted, and they can no longer feel the hairs; and this is the form of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle, and insert one silk thread of the same subtlety; then assemble the threads and join one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then arrange in the hunt another thin silk thread briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then put the patient's head on your lap; and be under the sun so that the works are declared, for it is a subtle and small work, then push the needle through all the chase to the root of the hair next to, and make it pierce the paper hastening as you move above the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it reaches the top of the chase, and push into the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs come forth all over the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the chase from below all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes forth from the pimple above and you see it with the sight of the eye; then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eyes and leave it two or three days, until the hair grows back to its place and the flesh forms a scab; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural beard, and lift it up with that one where you leave it, until it is stretched out and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pouring of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the pouring comes into the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or incision, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut open the wound, and loosen the lips of it, and put inside linen cloths, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. For if you do so, the disease will return worse than the first one; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or alethea and flaxseed cooked, and ointments made from daquilon melted in some oil, and wrap it in a cloth, and cure those.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care to ensure it does not heal in a way different from how it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing other than remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is below and which is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and cutting and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle with one double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce all the way to the right eyelid until the threads come out in two pieces of flesh; then remove the flesh above all the needle, and cut at one spatulate blade.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is necessary, that's good; if not, take one razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuts within the paper; and let the edges of the two incisions be at the two angles of the cut that you have made, so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has no name except "one Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are worn out below, from what is attached to the paper; then join the two severed parts and sew them with one thread of flax; then follow the cure with those medicines that we have said, and with cloths, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from incision or cutting or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what was said before; then sever between the two lips of a cloth, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an artifice of all their power so that they can bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in many ways similar to the paper above being bound with white of egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you insert the point of a razor below the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it to the pincers, until you cut what is at the spatulate blade, which is not too tight nor too loose, so that the patient cannot suffer if the spatulate blade is too tight or bleeds into the oil; and make your incision, from which you remove that assembled part, slightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and let the whole assembly be healed, and sometimes in the oil, salty water, and then lift it with sweet water and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a cloth of linen, and place on the oil moist flaxseed in abundance of yolk; and after the third day use vinegar and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the inflammation of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the inflammation is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moisture congealed, which when touched with iron and cooked at pincers, cannot be removed; and both kinds of inflammation begin near the great eyelid, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then you open the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then coil the inflammation at pincers with small double folds, and stretch it above; then take a needle and put one hair from horse, cow, or ox on it, along with a strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the inflammation, and make it pierce all the way to the needle, and tie the inflammation with a thread and stretch it above, and remove the remaining portion at the edge of the inflammation that comes from the prunele and the silk up to the chief; then cut off what remains in the root of the eyelid to the spatulate blade and the small forces, and leave the natural flesh or eyelid so that the body does not come forth with tears habitually; and sometimes the inflammation settles at the onyx alone, and on the thread, as we have said; then one removes all the spatulate soft from what is left:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et garde que the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prunelle is not pierced; and after the incision pour a little bit of burnt oil into the eye, and make a powder of litargire, and leave it until the next day; then cure what needs to be done so that it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot push the awl in, and the splinters cannot enter, many times this resemblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and it happens as I have counted in the division, and if you see it cover, then work on the patient's eye, and take the spatula lightly, and make an incision according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail off slowly, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the eye a powder made of litargire and red oil and burnt oil, and stop the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as a hot abscess, then drain it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts in the eye by great harm, then suspend it with a splinter, and cut off a part but not all, so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red oil made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the prunelle
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men sometimes grow red flesh, and cover the prunelle, and restrain above the papillae and turn them back behind, and seem like a rose of balaust; and the work is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you work on the eyes, and cut off all that flesh with suitable splinters for this, and sustain it by force; then cut off the first flesh, and go all the way cutting to the razor's edge, and take care not to bleach the eye at the operation; and make the incision of the spatula as we have said in the incision of the nail and with small forces, so that one takes away the scab, as the form after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then pour oil of burnt oil or distill red oil and similar corrosive medicines into the eye, and place a cotton cloth with egg white on top of the eye, so that it is secure from hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and blood flows forth, and you doubt hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the abscess with soothing things for hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do all the flesh which has grown in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is also necessary that you ease the cure of each weak eye by natural way; and by accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see that this member can suffer from that operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Scabs are red veins that are covered on the eye, and tolerate the sight's operation and weaken the eye all the time. It is necessary then at first that you look if the eye where the scab is, is sound, and there is no other disease except the scab; then coil it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your hand, then suspend those veins with all the splinter according to his wisdom, and be the splinters subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two splinters by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the forces of those veins subtly, and let the blood flow out hour after hour, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and take care not to bleach the eye with points of spatula; and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your operation so that you do not cut too much than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye green and red oil to corrupt what is left of the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all that in one hour, then make an application on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and are secure from hot abscess; then resume according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the abscess of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor calls it "arissati" abscess: when you cure it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in it that you cut into the abscess where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then take it out with all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of iron to one chief rent, and be pointed as a razor as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the surface is hardened, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is hardened, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not apostemed, and bad accidents come, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to bring back the abscess to the pit of the nose according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one force according to this form, and be the head of iron at three angles, and the handle be thinned down to the chief as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the eyelid, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the whole force until it pierces the bone and lets the patient feel through what the veins do if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the surface with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the surface, the matter flows out to the nose; and it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Quant the eyes appear to be full of pus in all and all, and it does not come from a disturbance or diminishment, then it is necessary that you lie the patient; then heal the wound, then apply poultices or a hot iron to help it heal; then put on top one layer made of aloe, encens, and sarcocolle, and then strain the eyes, and anoint them with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, and fold each into four parts, and then put one on top of the other according to what the eyes need; then strain by wrapping it with a strong bandage, and renew the poultices in order to help heal without causing harm; then remove the poultices and let the eyes be strained day and night, and if the layers become moist, then it is necessary that you strain them much; then remove the layer after day and night, and if you see the eyes repairing themselves, it is good; but if not, then renew the anointing and the cloths and the layer and the poultices until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Through the bursting of the conjunctival fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disturbances come to the conjunctival fabric, then it bursts open, and comes out in paper-like sheets as if a resin grain, and it is astonishing to see; therefore, if you see it covering, the work is such that you put an awl into the root of the part below just up to the part above, then put another awl where there is a double thread from the eyelid part; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its disposition; then cut the top of the double thread and tie one part of the conjunctiva around, and strain it well, then extract the awl and put on the oil a moist layer in abundance of egg white; and let it be until the threads cling with the conjunctiva, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the conjunctiva each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear swollen, then pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from the depth of the eye, and clear out the excess moisture and descend into the eyes, and enter soon after; then strain it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the bottom of the eye assembled in the eye, appearing like water flowing down, and it's not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and gently move it until you see the bottom coming up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and don't let it descend and be removed from sight, and let the patient see things as they usually do; and if it doesn't descend below, know that it's a flow of water, and if the descending of the bottom isn't arranged as we have said. Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make a small hole on the corneal tissue one spot at a time by continuing the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the crown, until the bottom emerges; and when it has emerged, then distill hot honey mixed with water or fenugreek into the eye, or boil honey and water together, and then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the tears of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of tears in our division, and what is necessary for piercing; so work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light due to the sun, and tie the good eye tightly; then put the paper on top of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left, or in your right hand if they are right; then take in your right hand if the eyes are left, or in your left hand if they are right, the instrument called "almagda"; then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a finger on the white part of the eye at the part of the minor eyelid; then put the almagda instrument virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prune up to the end of the nightshade; and that is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper due to the brightness of the corneal tissue, and then put the instrument just above or where the water is, and then express it below one way after another. If the water flows now, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again along the second path, put the force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and doesn't rise further, gently extract almagda by turning your hand slowly; then pour in a small amount of gemstone oil and leave it inside the eye. Then put on top of the eye estoupe or moist linen in rose water and in abundance of egg white, and bind with the good eye. As for us, and those who are of our time, we put on a comb made with abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctive alone, and don't go too far in, but make a fine line, then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a suitable bed, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and take light food, and don't move your head to the right or left, and be tied according to its disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the tie until the seventh day; and it is not necessary for you to do this during the cure or after the incision now, but rather delay it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if a pustule or boil comes up, then you should release the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the pustule; and when it is appeased, then release the sight and put on a face mask for one day to cover any rash, and be patient in that dark house. And then leave the house slowly and gradually, and convert back to your usual condition; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his land people pierce their almagda (a type of wart) with water, but I never saw anyone do this in our land nor did I ever read about it in books of old; and by chance this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of warts, because he who does not know them sees them; and they are properly of earth.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these warts are of the same subtlety, and the ends in three angles are watery.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time do the flesh on the nose become joined together in diverse ways, of which some appear like scorpions to many people; and if there are such or if it has a charm enchanted by foul color, and if it is soft and not enchanted. Then you should make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the juice onto those warts, and treat them fiercely; then take what you can bear to endure at the sharp subtle point of a part, until you know that that wart is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that you cannot remove, then open it with all .i. of the subtle instruments lightly, so that there is nothing left; and if without causing harm, or abscess opens, then cauterize as needed; and if these are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until the blood is staunched and all the warts are removed, then pour wine, oil, or vinegar onto the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose is open and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not flow as needed, know that there is a wart born in the bone above, for which instruments do not come to cut: then you must put one thread of linen, somewhat thick, into your hands, and tie each knot with at least one or less space; and place the patient's head on the thread at his power, and treat it with odorant until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do this to children at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do so; then hold the head that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth in the other hand, and know one after the other as you are with those who are on the thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that wart, then take away the warts, clean the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back on the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of wart; and then put a piece of cloth on the nose some days until it is healed, and if it needs medicines such as those, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purge the head, which distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or earth, resembling an open lamp like a cane, and conduct thus; and if you see, then make a closed cane, and the instruments full to purge the head; and have one band at the head to hold when heating oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose, and grows and becomes great in time, until it is visible to look at; and therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all impurities, then put the cautery or burning medicine on top; and if one delays cutting it as long as it is great, be wary if it is hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touchment, not of foul color, and you see that you can remove all of it, empty the patient's head and cut without fear, and cure the head with things restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, more than in some people. It is necessary then to do what happens to anyone, if you look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips into a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their color until they bleed, then bring together the two lips into a seam, and strain them, and powder with blood of dragon, and incense of burnt gum; and put on top of the powders a piece of emplaustre of strong or other emplaustre following, and leave it until it takes effect by itself, then cure with oil until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips abscesses hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each notch, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the lip after the incision of vitriol, until the blood is staunched; and then anoint with oil, and cure the lip with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a wart grows on the gums that the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you support it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on top of the wound vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders; and if that wart returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the sorors (sorores)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are assembled in the chief of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as corruption comes to the gum, and they are the teeth that stink; therefore it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his teeth be in thy sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness, and jaundice and other blemishes, until they are cleaned away; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it is good; but if not, then one renews the second day and the third, until you have removed all; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because those who pluck out the teeth to remove decayed teeth have different forms than those who remove between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with thee.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth's pain that you wait to draw it out as long as you can, for this should not be done quickly; for it is a very high substance so that there is no excuse for drawing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to draw out, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth's sensitivity. Many times the pain would drive the patient mad, and he would think it was the tooth of a saint, and would have a good tooth drawn out; and yet the pain does not depart from him because of this, until the bad thing is extracted, for we have already wanted to do this to those saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth's sensitivity, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a spatula all along the gumline strongly to protect the gums from all sides; then move it to your hands or use fine pincers at the first notch and notch, as long as it is well extracted, then secure the pincers well; and the patient's jaw should be held firmly between your knees, so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and then move it as you did first. And if the tooth is perforated and has a hole, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloth, where the holes are; and then strain it subtly with pincers, so that it does not break when straining; and it is very necessary to work carefully around the gumline to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and it will regrow in the patient through the malice of the root causing greater pains than the first. And be careful that you do not act like ignorant saints who, because of their haste and boldness, sometimes break the cart and do not bring what we have told; but they often bring great diseases by the roots that remain or by breaking the cart, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with vinegar, or vervain, and silk; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply a poultice of vitriol; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one should extract teeth first, are to be long-pointed and thick-handled, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be made of thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling out, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to hold firmly in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the pull, it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton swab on the area .i. day or ij., until the area is softened, then put in pincers called "algefri", with which the jaw seems to be a surgeon's; and they are made inside like a file, and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the cart entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is to know palying, of which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these things, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come after this:
