Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument that has two springs, of which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like great pincers, whose shape is this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be made so that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of cases, and if one breaks the cartilage or the other bones, or it can, then seek out the instruments that you need, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, whose shape is this:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the area with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then reduce it with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form and the shape is ugly, especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know whether the tooth is born after the tooth and is not in its proper place, and cannot be shaved or filed: then extract it; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is this, and which resembles a small beak, and be made of well-forged iron with a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping goes slowly and slowly in hands of days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it appears to be able to be filed, then file it with a similar file whose shape is this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth slowly and slowly in hands of days lightly, so that it does not move until it is trimmed; then make it even at the end with any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then file away the roughness as long as it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they are eating without it crumbling, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, but this does not work; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, for silver threads become green and rotten, but gold never changes; and the middle thread should neither be too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are misaligned, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the ligament between the false teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the area up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and carefully, so that it does not move; and make sure your ligature is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then file the threads with pincers, and assemble them, and re-point between the healthy tooth, and put it in such a way that it does not wound the tongue; then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, then restrain it with another thread; so it will remain and serve thus for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of aligning the two healthy teeth, and the two false ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Et when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and does not intervene except by someone who is wise and patient, and sometimes makes the shape of a whalebone tooth, and puts it where the defect is, and holds it tight like we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to bind the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from below the tongue or by natural birth; or by accident of a healed wound; and the works are such that you work on the patient's mouth and have their head in your care, and lift up the tongue; then bind the nervous ligament at length, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is stiffness or hardness, it is from sudden wound, so put in a compress and bind the ligament; and beware that the cut is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you have done this, then lift up the rosewater and vinegar mixture, or cold water, and place a linen tent under the tongue; and swab the patient each night so that the leeches cannot adhere. And if blood decoration comes, put it on the leech with vitriol powder; and if the blood increases, cauterize it at the slow fire cautery, which is good for this purpose; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it as being of fusse color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining into blenchor, and there is moisture, then put in a compress, and make a small poultice, and deliver from one side to the other; and if the blood increases at your work, put vitriol powder on top until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have done everything right; then lift up the rosewater and vinegar mixture, and cure with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there comes within the throat boils which are called "godath", and one properly calls them "the two almonds", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take heed: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and fusse color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of blood decoration; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would burst on its own; and if it is of white color bent, and the root is subtle, have the instrument ready to bind, but first look to see if the abscess has settled and is appeased. Then make the patient sit before the sun, and their eyes be in your care, and work on the mouth and take hold of the servant's hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, so that it forms; and it should be of silver or fine iron, as small as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a compress and insert it into the almond, and draw it up above as far as you can; and draw nothing else with it, then bind at the instrument, so that it forms, which seems like one force; and yet the head is bent, and one side to another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then bind it with pincers, so that it forms:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be torn from one side and the other; and when you have bound one of the almonds, then bind the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and hot and vinegar mixture, and if there is decoration of blood, gargle the patient with water or cooked grape pome husks, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so bind them then in this way as the two almonds are bound.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born within the throat, namely one abscess of small sense; and I had well closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the conduit which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained like that for one or two days. The abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two veins through the two outlets of the nose. I hastened then, and inserted a compress into one, and drew it up high, and pulled out a great deal of pus; then refilled the other side in the other outlet of the nose, and worked on the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that, I inserted the compress into those abscesses, and bound a part, and only a small amount of blood issued; and thus was unobstructed the conduit of the throat for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and ceased not to cut away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recrossed again, and filled up the space I had cleared out, until it became very large; then I bound it and cauterized it within the throat: thus it grew back again; and I departed from those parts, and left only as God did after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling descends to the vein, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is under a large and rounded one, it is called "vein". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the swelling abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to bind it; and the rounded one assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of white color or black, then it is necessary to avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger on the patient. It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, about its swelling and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument which we have made a note of before; then insert the compress into the vein, and draw it down below, and bind with one or two instruments as I have said in the incision of the almonds. And it is necessary not to bind more than the superfluity that is beyond natural term; for if you bind more, it will cause trouble to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of binding, then it is necessary to use a trick to cauterize with no fear. The manner of cauterization is hot water. It is that the patient puts their head in your care, and then presses their tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter on cautery, and confuses with live hot water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using the handle of this instrument, which forms:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put it in a place, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with hard earth, and inside the pot have one instrument shaved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the keys inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapour rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numb; after which it often starts again, until the eye dries, and beware that you do not make this at the beginning of the hot abscess's appearance, for many things happen then; and do not make this unless at the decline of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put a quill of egg inside it, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the quill of egg does not allow the vapour to weigh heavily on the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is applied to the throat or spine of a fish or any thing; so it is necessary that you try what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear and is returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit while the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is purged through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a lettuce root, or one piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it comes up, it will be strained, and then you will pull out; and if it does not come up with what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and have the head lifted upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all life depart from it, nor push the bone inside; and it is better for the patient to insert the instrument, because then or the thing is purged; if they insert it downward, or pull it out slowly with all the instrument equal, until it is pulled out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the snot from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	At no time is the snot medicated, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, then press the tongue on the instrument that I told you. And if you see the snot, pull it out slowly with one small hook or delicate forceps suitable for this. And if this is not worth it, take a curved tube and insert it into the throat of the patient, then put a hot iron at the end of the tube and do it often. And if the patient is kept in water all day, then take a full view of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it out without swallowing, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the snot feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asefetide at the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will surely come out. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot where there are live coals, and let the top be covered with a pierced cloth, and in that perforation put the keys of the instrument; then pour your fumigation into it, and have the patient place the head of the tube in their mouth, and close their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to the snot; and the snot will now fall, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and ales, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary that it come out through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one pulls out the snot is like this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps suitable for entering the throat; and it has a resemblance to a bird's beak, and has asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and behold the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings forth hereafter from one and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; and it is in two manners by which the one is similar itself, and that which holds moisture. And the second manner is for those that are on the bone or in the flesh. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the bone that are charred are different from those that come into joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the pus is mature according to its completion; and there are others that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard and do not die according to their completion, like those that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves them so long that they are putrid all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is on the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is matured, it will harm the principal member; or if it is on the foundation, one should pierce it immediately after it has died; and it is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is on the foundation, lest it burst forth and become a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess when it has died according to its completion, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the departures of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and of swelling and disquieting of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation or more depending on the location of the abscess, and where it appears to be; and the perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, and nerves, and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pleasure.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are pleasurable, according to that member. And when abscesses are in charred areas, it is better to wait until they are confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before then, the body will be filled with a great deal of foul matter; and by chance, the lips and the surrounding area may become hardened. And there are some abscesses that should be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cil who have not a chief, if it be aposteme soft superficial, it is necessary that you pierce calmly; and when the apostemes are great, and it has coiled great bowe, and you pierce, then do not draw all the bowe in that hour, but only part of it; then stop the aposteme just until the next day, then draw out nothing further from there; do this by many times with ease, until the bowe is altogether gone; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor leu decorrant par maintes fois.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses; and I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Wherever a sore comes on the head, it is small abscesses and are ways of ours that are in fabric, just as a tailor works with silk; and there are many similarities. Some are fatty and similar to those with moisture like pustules; and some are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make it contrary. And the works of cutting are such that you test every .i. instrument that is called "entromissoire", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, then let it dry above the long one. And when the moisture is gone, then scrape off without leaving anything; for it will return again if you leave anything behind; then plunge cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and soap, and fill the wound, and let it stay until the next day; and that which remains of the night. And then restart the cotton, just as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night; then cure the wound with oil as necessary, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds one fat night, then cut into according to this form, from above; and throw away your scraps, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in drawing out what lies within; and if the artery makes it contrary, do what I told you afterwards. And likewise do with the abscess if it is stony, and of cutting and curing just as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony abscess and the moist one is lighter, for they contain little blood. And if there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and I saw one abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a dry, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if anyone had tried to open it, they would have made a wound as if from a stone. In other abscesses coming on the head, except those that come on the heads of children and the roots of ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent point, in order to let the pus issue; and cure them as needed.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the shoulders, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are connected one with another. And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, just as the night and the abscess of the head, just as we have said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see one with good disposition for cutting, and is similar in color to the body, and quiet on each side, and is not inflamed at the neck or artery or conduit, and is not deep; then it is necessary to cut above, and scrape off each part, and are the two lips of the wound, if you need them, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and take little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor be the spatula awkwardly or cutting, lest your hands escape, and do not see too far ahead, lest you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you finish, then put vitriol broth or some powders that remain blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; then look at your index to see if there are any small scrofulas remaining, cut them and scrape them off. And if there is a great vein in the root of the scrofula, then do not need to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall away harmlessly; then fill the wound with old cotton plunged in Egyptian oil, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole scrofula, then it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any superfluity due to the greatness of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand how to cut at its root and draw out what remains, and sew it as we have said. Those scrofulas that retain superfluity, burst open where it appears moist; and burst forth in this way like the one mentioned before, depending on it; then administer tentatives with oil and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then cure it with oil anointing flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have scabies, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "epiglote" be opened; and one does not make aid by these means, because all the veins and the pomegranate of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pomegranate, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the syphilitic sore, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and that one is suitable for the section of the epiglote so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire circumference, then cuts the flesh as far as it reaches the channel; and stop the flow of blood, if you see anything, and then cut out the syphilitic sore, just as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the flesh of the channel which bursts forth through the torn ligament and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound remain open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care, and sew all around without leaving any cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Also it is said that one should not do this just yet until the throat is entirely swelled, and the patient is judged to be on the point of death, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this reason the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or in four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they command to sew up the wound and heal it, until it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one dagger and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the veins of the throat.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I saw well that she had not cut the vein nor conducted it far from the throat, and the veins were flowing freely through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was well.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the maiden that she regained her voice, and returned to her usual condition after this.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting off the epiglottis there is no need to be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in a greenish color, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is like fatty tumors, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not necessary to operate unless the one that is small is fiery, and he proves and searches through all the entrails;
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like a fat lump, and cannot be drawn by any vein, then cut it off, just as one cuts out the fat, and treat it with all its folds, if there is no other way.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and cure it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	of the fat
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of fat that I will tell you all about their likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary for me to say the whole difference that is between fat and abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, holding fast until the ebullition has passed, and the corruption is completed; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the fat there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains one sac that is its own pouch and is according to the color of the flesh, and begins just like a green abscess, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two likenesses, either fat or moist, and much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the fat, that you examine and inquire first through all the instruments called "entrails", according to what its form will be or chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of fat is that you take or the wettest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers and fingers, until you know that the instruments have pierced through to the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the entrails, and take care in what jumps forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moist part is corrupt, whether it has any color, then treat it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after extracting the entrails no moist part comes, know that it is fat, then treat it by scoring and pinching it, and scrape it lightly from each side and take care of the coat where it lies so that you can treat the fat with it.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot treat it healthy, then cut it into pieces so that there is nothing left.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, then the fat will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if even a small part remains and the blood grieves you, then apply the wound with some corrosive powders, and restrain the wound, and put on soothing things to the hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the fat is large, then sew up the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what grows flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another thing that is contrary to you, or if you hurry and apply the lead of vitriol powder, and let it be for two days or three, until the wound purrs, and rest the ebullition of blood; then return to cutting off what remains of the fat.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the entrails instruments, and they are in three manners: great, middle, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three ways: great, middle, and small, to search for abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews suture holes, and they are of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most proven to find black pocks to search for the abscesses of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are in three manners: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the needles are of many likenesses, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and there are needles that have two black pocks of three manners.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are needles that have three black pocks, and they are also of three manners; and there are needles that have two black pocks, and single needles with one black pock, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these needles that we use are cutting ones, and there are some that do not cut much more than one side, with which we scrape off the fat, so that we do not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these intervening things are the bandages replied in rags, so that the patient does not perceive anything at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and there are three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use more than in a well-oiled joint, such as knees, and arms, and shoulders, and at angles, and in similar joints;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the tips of fingers, according to this form, with which one staunches blood;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals with completeness of veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to do according to this form of this line up to the 7th;
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicated charcoal, then bring together the two lips of the wound to the seam, and cure it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags downward, and is puffed up because of its size like it has in women, then make two cuts above it, through two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is joined to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b up to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and all that is necessary for the cure, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the discharging of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with wet cotton in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it so that it mingles with the remaining fat and oil, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the hips
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the hips are types of hard scrofulas with ridges, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the swelling that is in the abscess has gone down, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar kind to scrofulas, then do it as we have said in incisions for scrofulas, and if the wound swells, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is sewn up, then many times abscesses come forth, and just as it happens with an inflated vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep by far;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it in your abdomen, then you feel a strangeness; and when it is due to the vein, then there is pus appearing outside;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut into this abscess, and especially when it is under the hips and shoulders and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary therefore to avoid the treatment of fire, and he who is at the head should also avoid it, and in that which is due to an inflated artery, make an incision above the skin as long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the shape like a needle, and carefully part the artery from the surrounding tissue, until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle underneath one edge, and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then tie off the place between the two ties with a small instrument so that the blood that is there issues forth, and the abscess be relieved.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that discharges swelling, until the tie falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply ointment as needed, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then it is necessary that you paint with your hand all that you can of the abscess on the entire skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce through, and have one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or tie one of the two parts to the two knots of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not come out far enough, then rebute another needle at all one thread under all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess flows out, then cut the excess of fat and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses on the knees
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come from the artery and vein, abscesses on the knees come when they are fatigued or from too much heavy labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often on the shoulders and knees and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it occurs in multiple dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one strains strongly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the fat.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it hurts all around, and does not go forward or backward, nor above or below, and the one in joints should not be cut with iron at all: by chance there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one on the head or forehead, make the skin split open.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then take hold of it with tweezers and cut off its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is great, then suspend it to the splint, and flay it, then remove the flesh and stitch the wound at the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of big boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	It sometimes happens in bellies and not elsewhere at all, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to them, and the roots are subtle, and the head big; and there are some small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and were oozing moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6, and the work of incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the articular flesh is white and moist and of subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if you cut it with a spatula that is large, and the cautery with fire is before you. For when cutting comes many times too great bleeding of blood, and if the blood overflows, then hurry to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient espousing and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one piece of linen well made, and bind the articular flesh as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the linen thread until it cuts through the articular flesh, and choose by its sense work; and if the roots are large, then be afraid to cut too much for the belly, but you can well cut half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not relapse; then treat the wound, and take care that you do not cut through the flesh which is of mixed color, and of poor sense, and with no regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enchanced, and I will come to the treatment of chancres here after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery of wound or incision of syphilitic sore, and it is on the belly and in some of the boils, just as it happens in other ulcers, or from blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is due to the ulcer of syphilis and by the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press it at its sides it swells up, and then returns, and by chance it becomes hard, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and from great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, not at all constraining; and if it is due to blood, then it opens by these signs of the large and hard abscess, and fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, then it is sore when touched, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of an artery, or a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	So it is necessary to leave the wound alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to intestine or pus, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his bowels, and be stretched out straight, then sign around all the boil.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit comfortably between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have signed with all the spatula.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then expose half of the abscess above to the great splint;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread, or with a firm silk cord, and let the knot be securely fastened.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the half of the abscess extended above the bandage, and put your finger's index, and try to loosen the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the bandage, then loose it, and push the intestine back into the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the pus, take it with the spatula, and cut off the superfluity;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein gives you trouble, go around it nicely, then come back to your work and take two needles, and put two fine threads on them, and pass the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in three places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the place be such that it can open, and choose the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and open, then treat it as needed, and dry the abscess as we have said.
