et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of chancres
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the likenesses of chancres, and how one should work with medicines, and how one must avoid iron treatment; and we say that chancres are born in the womb, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients say that when chancres are on the skin or in a place where it can be scratched like chancres which are in the armpits, and in the groin, and in similar places, one must completely remove it when it begins; and when it is great and old, then it is not necessary to approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black coles once or twice; then make them healthy if they have manifest repletion; then dress the patient's wound well to do the work; then throw away your splints or chancres, and clean it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow fully, and press the wound gently with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: it is said to be clear; and one should not touch with iron in these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and hypsarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore, when you medicate this likeness of dropsy called "clear" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then look if the patient is weak or has another disease than dropsy, such as all stomach trouble and similar things; do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient in good health, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then thus proceed.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Hold the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press upon the belly by pushing out water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the spineless thorn according to this form: And be cutting into two parts to a point, yet not so much that it may reach as far as the intestine when you insert it, nor can it harm.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is flowing towards the intestines: if so, it is necessary that you cut above the mouth .iii. inches from below on the edge; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision will be on the left side of the mouth .iii. inches; and if it is due to mucus, then it will be on the right side, and it is not necessary that the patient lies above the incision so that superfluities do not flow towards that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and bind it, and lift your hand to all the thorn between the skin and the fatty tissue just as when shearing to the quantity of a fingernail or around; then pierce the fatty tissue until the thorn comes to the right width, and that is the sign of water; then treat the wound, and insert this instrument according to its form: And it resembles a silver thread, subtle and made of iron or lead, with a small hole in the lower part; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the keys are cut like a feather, and that is the form of the incision by which writers fashion the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now descends on the instrument; empty then one-third or two-thirds of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or they may fall unconscious, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of their vigor, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the key that closes the hole which is above the fatty tissue, about which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw off a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this day after day, and be careful not to drain more than a small amount of water. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave too much water, it will cause them to suffer from heat stroke or sunstroke, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and if they become thirsty; and treat with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach, liver, and spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born who do not have a small hole in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. It is necessary that he be pierced at once with all .i. thorn very subtle according to this form: then put one small plug of lead into the hole and tie it and keep it thus for three days or four; and when he wants to urinate, take off the plug, let him urinate, and then put it back; and by chance it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave the plug closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who have a small hole are treated with lead plugs, as we said, and it will expand. Those who do not have the hole in its place are harmed, for no one is born with the hole at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis high; and they cannot flow because the matter cannot come all the way to the end, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, and then the top of the penis is bent and cut like the shape of a pen nib, so that the hole opens in its place, as it should; and be careful not to disturb the blood that comes out many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops bleeding, and cure the wound until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	These pustules often come on the penis, and it is a foul appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; therefore, take them at one subtle poultice, and cut and clean all of them, then apply wet cotton in Egyptian ointment; then treat with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pustule is malignant, with putrid color and odor, it is necessary that you apply a cautery. When you have cut it open, and if the pustule is on the skin of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the pustule which is inside first; and when it is bound up, then treat the outside. For if you treat them together, the wound of the penis will not be secure, and there will be blackness and corruption in its place and on the coition; therefore, seek out all that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice made from the rind of pomegranates and vetches, and then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterizers help with two dispositions together: namely, with bleeding and corruption; and if the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put a lead tube in the penis of the patient and make him urinate between his legs; and when the foreskin at the head of the penis has been flayed off, which has not been circumcised, or if there is a wound or aposteme, then it is necessary that you circumcise with a sharp instrument, so that the foreskin is detached and the penis is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	et se c'est grief chose de deviser ceu, if it is a grievous thing to discuss this
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the severing of continuity like other wounds; however, when we do this work by our own desire and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greatest part of masters and seniors who performed circumcision around one inch, and with forces, and all a new needle; it would be cut because there are two layers, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is to cut again, and there is double pain, and at the purification which is above the skin is not assuredly secure the point of the member; and at the purification of the wound by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times it happens thus that they have no need for purification and I want this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force, I have found the goodness of experience, for the forces cut equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, so it cuts equally well in one stroke with all the strength of the tendons; but let the thread be well strained around the skin; and as for the manner of the first operation, it is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing anything to him except tying the thread around the penis only, and then let it sit in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it rest between your hands straight and put the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and pull it up as high as the head of the penis is; then clean well the dirt that has assembled there, then tie a double thread signet, then tie underneath one foot to another link; and hold with two thumbs by the second binding to the pouch and to the left index, and cut between the two links, then lift the skin above hastily and pull the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for it is the mothers; and put powder on top and on top another layer of powdered egg yolk cooked with rose water, mixed with good and fresh olive oil, and leave it on until the next day, and then cure with another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: two fingers should be held and should be pressing, and they should be equal to the width of a thumb.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the blood flows into the incision; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, so that the lump makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is appeased, and lightly scrape; then cut as you can move, and be careful of the part of the penis, for it will harm nothing.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wound with soothing powder, as we have said to treat powders, and if you cut too much from the skin, and it goes above, it will harm nothing; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the kidney stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone in the groin or in the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and have his feet placed on the back, and extend his belly from above the back to the part below, and restrain the patient's body as much as he can; and then constraining the neck of the bladder to express the stone above, whereby the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", whereby there is this form: and it should be made of thin silver hair, like the feathers of a bird; and it should be one and a half palms long, and should be subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of urine issue is that you take a double thread, and tie one end to the head of a piece of wool or cotton, and insert the other end into the siringue; and cut off the excess thread so that it fits snugly at the head of the siringue, then anoint the siringue with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tea water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then place the siringue gently into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis above towards the mouth; then insert the siringue forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel come close to the empty thing, and that is not done according to this order unless the guide or channel through which it goes is twisted; then stretch the thread all along the wool piece and piece, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the siringue until the bladder is emptied, and have the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bleedings or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it dripping with waters and medicines, then do with all the instrument that is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are trimmed so that the medicine flows well without adding anything to the penis, if we can then draw out the moisture and insert it when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture, and pull out what is inside it; if you pull out the moisture through the catheter, then push strongly the piston inside; then the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: thus it is
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of archaic; and the head is higher; and underneath one breast or the cord falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture which you see enemas the bladder, then tie between two breasts with a good double thread, and heat one pouch with that moisture on the fire; then pour the head of the enema into the sheath; then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture beneficially, until the patient feels that that moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put in a strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles a tile, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand so that the moisture comes out at the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between the stoned abscesses as regards rains, and all signs, and which kind of stone one should work on; and in the bladder, and in the sheath; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stoned in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hare-like, and the patient's sheath swells, and he pees many times, and then becomes inflamed; and many of these stones are formed at the foundations; and it is lighter to heal children until they are three years old, and it is much more grievous in old men, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those with a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines. For sometimes it hinders seeking out the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move him downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes slides from above; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hasten now to cut on the stone. And if it does not fall at all when touched, then moisten your two middle fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your two outer fingers, if the patient is a young adult; and pour it into his foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, then bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it on your finger, and push it forward outside where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the skin above in height, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the skin on the part where one makes the incision; then put in the spatula copant, which is this form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make a slit between what is between the skin and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left naively; and be straight on the stone, and your two fingers be beside the foundation, and be the incision of the traverse so that it be wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	In case the press is made with the fingers that are at the foundation, it may jump forth too quickly; and know that there are such stones which have angles and margins: it is hard to get out; and if one is found which is soft, resembling a horn, and rounded, whose issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that one then where it has angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump forth, it is necessary that you strain upon the forceps which are like a file at the head, in order to press the stone so that it does not escape; or put beneath the one instrument a subtle curved corbel at the head; and if you cannot shape it thus, then widen one pouch the perforation, and if the sand decorticates, then strain it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, then put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove it forth, and the small ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, then you must split it, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out suddenly below where the flesh cannot heal; but nonetheless strive to extract it, or to break it with forceps, as long as you take it apart piece by piece.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, then apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put over it one damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot aposteme; then revitalize the patient on his back, and do not untie the band until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, then raise the patient very well with oil and water, and then cure him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if apostemes, boils, and congealments of blood appear in the wound and corrosion, and it is retained by the urine which is gathered in such a way that it does not flow out with the urine: then put your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and ruin it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound with water and egg white and vinegar, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, you bind his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the bed.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the sheath, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out; then cure him as I say, and cut the skin many times, or excuse yourself from cutting because of this cure. I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and be fixed at three angles in one handle:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Here is the translation of the first sentence:
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	et if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then take one thread under the stone and another above, then make the stick end just between the two threads, then pull out the thread, loosen the ligament, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There often happens that the stone is inserted in women, and if it ever does, it is a grievous cure, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of surgery; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more inward than the stone of the man, therefore it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you take a midwife who knows well, and when you find one, you will know, and if you do not find one, just as much to get one skilled castor; and the present one should be a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order from the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to thrust her husband's thing or foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her husband's thing, and command her to thrust her husband's thing into the wound, and press her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the con, there where it appears in its apparel, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her husband's thing above or below the stone, and make the incision the first time small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then thrust the right in the incision, if you feel the stone so far into the wound that the stone can come out further, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and great and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges; thus know the likenesses to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood flows, then put vitriol powder in its place, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then come back to your work, until the stone is out, and have instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood flows and it is from the artery that was cut, then put powder on the place and strain of tents and bandages, and do not continue with this, and leave the stone alone and do not touch it again, lest by chance the patient would die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the place is clean, then come back to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramica aquosa is nothing else than a gathering of moisture or white fluid, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, as if it were another egg; and it's the skin of the testicle between the white syphac that we have said; and this does not happen unless one is not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramica is due to weakness that comes from the testicles, and it spreads that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it's declining to yellow, or it's without red, or black, or watered whites, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is white syphac that we have said, it is a swelling, a long one like the figure of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, it is a swelling with a part of the egg, and for this one thinks that it's another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syphac, you will know well; then when you see what color the moisture is, try everything that can be done to the surrounding quadrature, so that the shape is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the surrounding quadrature, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, then it is necessary that the patient be healed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then bind him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on her left side, and command the minister to sit on her right side, and extend the stick to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left, and cut the skin of the testicles in between the long ones until just below the nail, and make your incision entirely straight in cutting through the skin of the testicles just up to the white syphac, and scrape it subtly according to our power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the white syphac plain with water to one large pore, and draw out all the water, and then put in your needles, and stretch the white syphac upwards; and do not touch the skin of the testicles, but only the white syphac itself; cut it whole or in pieces, namely the side of it subtly, lest if you do not cut it well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg jumps out of your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white syphac; then join the two flaps of the skin of the testicles with a suture, and then cure it as you would other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you lift up the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the corruption of blood; then cut off the testicle to all the suspended part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two ramices; then cut off the other part similarly to how you did the first one, and wash away the blood, and put a moist poultice of rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put away another damp wool cloth in wine and oil, and put on the two cones, and put on double cloths, and tie it up to all the bandage that is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and stuff them with wool yarn according to this likeness and be sewn together in the girdle of the braies, and one of the straps takes up on the foundation just to the back, and the other at the part of the pointing; and the other chief on the two armpits, and be all assembled into the restraint of the belt buckle.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this medicine of cautery is done in place of iron surgery, and it is that you take one subtle surgical instrument, and cut the skin of the cones, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scab that contains water is uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white scab into little holes, and scrape it off with this subtle hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut in all the ways you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is more safe; and take care of avoiding decoration with blood, and more so than the works of surgery.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing else makes you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or another thing, then care for what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer a perfusion, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the ramica water is ready,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so make the patient sit on a low stool; then pierce the abscess in the part below all the way to the broad spatium, and put the perfusion through the length of the body; and be wide the holes, so that all the water can flow freely.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining water flow freely, then care for it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you insert a probe or instrument used for drawing off the water from dropsy, as described above; and widen one poultice the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after eight months or so, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cones
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this chapter there are more fears and dispositions, therefore it seems to me that one should not leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the cones; and this is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive bitter and watery humor that spreads to the cones, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find a pain, and is an heavy abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance some heavy abscesses are painful and piercing, and of foul color, and sometimes comes from a blockage of an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to a blockage of an artery, then it is known by the hot abscess, when you press it at your elbow.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not right that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made of swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of touching the elbow.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well perform surgery on this likeness, and on the other veins;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the cones, then raise the yolk high, and draw out the white scab, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the yolk is already solid with these veins, then it is necessary that you draw out the yolk and the skin.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is inflamed on the scab, or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and cut it again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the vein is in the lower part, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and draw out the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, then dress the wound with damp wool cloth in rose oil and wine, and care for it with other cares until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a bunch, with the softening of the cones,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the patient grievously complains when walking.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure for this disease is just as fearful as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a low stool, then place the suspensory of the cones downward at your elbow.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the penis, and bind them with strips, and extend them properly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut at the spatium trenchant, a broad passage in the middle of the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape off each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are on the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert an awl where there is a doubled thread, and bind it to the first place where the blood has flowed, and bind it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then dress the wound as with others that are not yet bound together, so that no vessel bleeds that nourishes one of the cones.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come blood, then it is necessary to draw out the cones from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and become dry and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the corruption of the scab
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this chapter are by the section that comes from the scab, or the extension above the belly in the part of the armpits, therefore the intestines descend into that corruption at one of the cones.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this corruption is from the scab, or from its extension, and comes in these two manners of many causes: by percussion, by jumping, by roaring, by lifting a heavy load, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of syphilis, if it is that it has a little and a little, in long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal right up to the very front, because the syphilis presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of syphilis, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses have diverse appearances, just below the skin, and this is because of the issue from the intestine and the body being overcome by the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at times the ulcers go down to the intestine, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, where there is fear, therefore one must take precautions.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of working is that you instruct the patient to reach inside the wound with his hand and try to get into the intestine if he can.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be steady on his neck between your hands, and lift up the ribs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then raise the kerchief above, and cut all the skin of the scrotum along its length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push the flesh of the abdomen into a bag according to what you need to open up the wound, and make it such that the bone can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape off the syphilis that is under the skin of the scrotum, until the white hard syphilis is uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then put your two fingers in the place where the scrotum ends, between the white hard syphilis that is under the skin of the testicle and the second syphilis.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and part what is behind the testicle, and between the second syphilis; and then move your right hand into the skin of the scrotum, and raise the white hard syphilis high up to your left hand, and lift the testicle away from all the syphilis towards the abdomen.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle up high and release what is above the bond.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around or white hard syphilis, and if you find anything, then push it into the abdomen below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with which there is 10 threads made of 1 thread, and insert it into the back part of the syphilis, which is after the skin of the scrotum; then cut the strings that appear as threads, until there are 4 threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the syphilis, which we have said is under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong bond of 2 parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the strings of threads and bind them together with a bond of 2 parts, so that no vessels that nourish it can enter in there, lest the abscess does not become worse.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the bandage on top of the bond according to the first long bond with 2 fingers, and after these 2 bonds leave a gap from the syphilis that is under the skin of the scrotum equal to the width of one finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that, do the same according to the roundness that the testicle bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the scrotum, until it is equal to the natural shape and size, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moistened linen dipped in oil to the wounds, and put on the bandage that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes it is necessary to cautery the white hard syphilis that we have said, after incision, due to fear of excessive bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the bandage on until it falls off by itself; and if it takes too long to fall off, then wash with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls off.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment by fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancient ones say that it is done in such a way as the remedy which is together with the vein, in the same manner that you bind the vessels, after cutting above and gently below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of one who works, until the vessels bleed; and then cure it as we have said, until he is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes comes rupture in the groin, as we have said, and open up the wound; and none of the intestines descend to the scrotum, and if any do descend, it is little, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if he remains too long in this position, the wound or syphilis grows, until the intestine descends.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the syphilis that is in the groin, as we have said, for it spreads out, then becomes softened and inflamed the wound and opens up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is done by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is not cured by fire in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies comfortably on his back between your hands, then cut the wound of the inflamed rupture from wide to narrow according to the length of 3 fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the syphilis that is under the skin which follows it, and take the rod and place it on top of the wound that appears from the syphilis.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it all the way to the bottom of the abdomen, then cut the two wounds that appear from the syphilis on top of the head of the rod, and cut one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	and then extract the head of the rod, and do not cut the syphilis nor extend the testicle, or any other thing, as I have made you aware in the cure of the remedy for the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and then treat it with the treatment for wounds. And when you cut the strings, have a nurse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilis is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is more effective in this wound, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men, because the contents inside are softened, and it is visible; and when one wants to cure it, one must make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin above the natural skin; then assemble the two lips into a seam, and if you see fit, cut off the excess of the soft skin at 3 or 4 seams; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds, until he is healed, and the thread falls.
dou chastrement	The punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The punishment is reckoned in our law, and it would please me that I not speak of it at all in this book; and it is only necessary for two purposes: one is that the physicians respond to questions about it when asked, and provide a cure; and the other, because we often need to chastise certain beasts to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts. I say therefore that punishment is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one where we do it by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then we take them in hand until they are remitted and you no longer feel them. About the castration of beasts: it is necessary that you grasp the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut above each ball once when you have well bled them; and I leave some space between the syphac and the subtle syphac which is on the vas deferens; and this manner of punishment is milder than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction some thing from the testicles remains by chance, whereby the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is in two ways like a man: one way is when between the two testicles appears as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes it urinates in court. And the other manner is in women, and it has on the fingernail as much as a penis and two testicles. And the cure for man and woman is that you cut off the excess skin all around, and cure it like other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the uterus
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The uterus is a thickened skin over the natural part, as much as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the cure. It is necessary that you grasp the superfluity of the uterus with your hand or forceps, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep in the flesh, lest bleeding occurs, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and there is another wound that arises at the mouth of the womb, and is filled, and by chance jumps forth, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and therefore they called it "cow disease" in olden times. It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said about the uterus, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of the hare-lipped
