Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	The hare-lipped is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the lip is small; and it is a natural condition, or an accident caused by disease that has occurred; or it is due to a thickened skin, or from the subtle syphac or espace, and is done in depth in the womb, or in the sides, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and by chance having flowers; and knowledge of this is by the inspection of the belly. If the swelling is apparent, then it goes to your fingers or the right. If it is from the subtle syphac, and it is near the two kidneys, you should hurry, and do as follows: place your two fingers together, and the woman should sit on her back, spreading her legs; then the two kidneys are formed, until the subtleties of the syphac are released, and the swelling is over; then take linen, and soak it in oil, and put it on the wound, and make the woman lie at home each day, so that she cannot solder. And if the syphac is hard and espace, you should cut it with a spatula like the leaf of myrtle. If the swelling is from born flesh, then suspend it to the forceps and cut it; and have medicines that stop blood, such as alum, dragon's blood, incense, and together with many eggs; then administer a bandage made of cloth wide enough so that the wound cannot solder; and thus be long-lasting, and administer another tent made of dry linen; then be cured by other treatments until it is healed. And when flesh is born in the womb, you should cut it according to this manner, unless it is an enchanted aposteme. For the aposteme that is enchanted in the womb should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not normally close, and when they are old they become thickened; and we have said in the division what their appearances and signs are, and I will say here those which receive a cure. I say that hemorrhoids and thickening, when they are deep in the womb, and there is no sensation of pain, are not curable by fire. Those that are at the mouth of the womb can be felt, and are those that can be cured. It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then make the thickened part into tongs, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and apple bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, then apply poultices to the back and breasts with no fire; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the wound. And when the aposteme subsides, cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough head, so it should be cut as I said about thickening; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of apostemes of the womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of apostemes come to the womb, such as chancre and pierous aposteme and herpes and swelling and fistulae and hemorrhoids and hot aposteme, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. It is necessary then that I say about the hot aposteme that comes to the womb, which is not one of the apostemes that are closed up with a bow; and if you want to know how to work with fire, look at whether the aposteme is agitated in its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it. Then don't hurry to cut it, but let it heal until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools or she reclines, and lean back onto her back and stretch out her legs away from the leg; and spread her thighs apart, and put her arms under her knees, and tie them well with a good cord; then place the birthing instrument towards the right side, and administer the instrument that is used to open the womb, so that the form comes forth; and it is necessary that when you are administering this instrument, you mark the first line on it to know the depth of the womb, so that what enters the instrument does not come deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the womb with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause her pain; and it is necessary to put the handle of the instrument on top and hold onto the instrument. And when the aposteme appears, and one makes a gentle motion with the hand, it is necessary to cut it at the head, with a spatula made like a lettuce leaf; and when the bowels are empty, it is necessary that you put a moist poultice in oil or rosewater on the wound, or in oil that has been cooked; and place the poultice above the wound at the bottom of the womb, and on top of the marris and on the elbow linen clean soaked in water or marshmallows are cooked; then cure it after two days with ointment suitable to what I have said, until it is healed.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs; that is when you see the woman leaning forward and desiring to push; then the child hastens to come out forthwith; then you should know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is below his head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on her belly so that the child comes out soon; for when it descends above his head, the secondine is with him, and the excesses of the mother are purged by good purging; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it sometimes comes on its feet, or excessive in the body or shoulder, or hands, or on the belly, or some other place, and is converted by chance on his neck, and by other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out above his head in natural issue, and the woman gives birth grievously, and her virtues are weak, then make her sit on a stool or have women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek cooked, and then give the midwife a small spatula-shaped instrument, as shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the afterbirth, and push with one finger as much as the moistors which are inside burst forth; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to purge the woman with fenugreek and oil of sesame; then make her take breath and stretch out in a comfortable position, and keep her mouth and nose shut for an hour: thus now the child is delivered. And if the two hands come forth, it is necessary that you gently guide them in and out; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a stool, and lift up her feet high; then set the stool down on the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall over; and if the hands cannot enter and the child dies, cut off the hands at the knife that is placed before, and extract the child, and guide it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it a little bit and a little bit until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and stretch it a little bit and a little bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can he jump just to his thighs, if the mother is commanded to press, and she takes breath in a comfortable position;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps too far, may God help.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not too far as we have said, then turn it a little bit and a little bit until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily fixed.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take fenugreek powder, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the woman's nature inside and outside with this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in cold water up to her navel.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, put a mire collar on her and place it underneath, and let her stay for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her take breath and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press the belly, for now the child is jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child from its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then place the midwife's hands on it a little bit and a little bit;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be careful with its neck, and let its feet hang down below, and be placed on one bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend its hands a little bit and a little bit, and then press its hands on the belly, and remove the pillows underneath until it is straightened up;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and shape them properly, then shape the belly upwards, then put your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and gently lift the child a little bit and a little bit; and command the woman to take hold until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes forth with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed, and straighten out her legs properly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the fenugreek that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a stool, and study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and gently lift the child according to its natural figure, and make her take breath, and command that she take hold until the child comes forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and having spread out its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary that the midwife takes hold of its hand, then turns it a little bit and a little bit, and gently lifts it.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then put on the natural powder of fenugreek and oil, as we have said, and command that she move a little bit and a little bit.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a stool, and command that she take hold; and make her take breath.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner with all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this way to all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with one finger until the moistors are empty.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child is placed on its face and neck, then cut from the mouth so that it is not retained, and kill the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as is necessary, and command the woman to take hold at times:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come forth easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are unusual things, and do not live if they do not have a name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the sac that divides them, which is connected to the mouth.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come forth naturally like all others under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come forth with difficulty, then the treatment is as we have said, and be subtle in manner, and do quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is of use for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb in number one, or two, or three, or four, or five, or six, or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of an infant by the measurement of wise glory,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the doctor knows all this, for by chance similar things happen to him;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman who has given birth to a dead child or miscarriage, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to work by hand;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know if the woman has a healthy disposition and does not have an accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the attendant takes hold of the woman by two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated with the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oil mixed with alum and fenugreek and flaxseed, then the doctor oils his hands with these oils and mixtures;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then pour them into the womb lightly, then take one or two of those that are suitable for this use,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and watch carefully to see if the child is formed and descends onto her head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you insert the cord in her ears or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or in the navel or near the ribs;
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on foot, then tie or prick it and make it come to the sides slowly;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the cord in his right hand and puts the curve between his left hand's fingers, and pours it all into his hand lightly, and inserts the cord into one of those places we have said until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the cord:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert another cord in front of one, or the third that you have need for, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, so that the cords are bitten to hold in place, as is the form;
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then the doctor oils some of his fingers with oil and pours it into that part, and treats the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there is no part left, then put this cord or more in a higher place, and do so until it all comes forth completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back by stretching;
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so it is necessary that you wrap it on a cloth, so that it all comes out;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cut at the joint of the foot or toe, and thus it is necessary that you do the same in the other hand, and with two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is strained in the issue, or it has a sharp-angled skull assembled;
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	so it is necessary that you insert the spatula-shaped spine between your fingers and shape the head and extract the liquid;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it with the instrument which is called "almidach", by which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus do the same if the child has a great natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat the bones with pincers,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps out and it is strained at the navel, then be split, until the moisture that is in the issue comes forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is inflated in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you make a hole until the moisture runs;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is gentle, and the direction to the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is strained in the belly or navel, then it is necessary that you extract it onto a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and shape the belly or navel until the moisture that is there runs.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if other members are missing, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then the doctor puts his hand into the womb to the depth of the womb, and treats it up to the mouth of the womb.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he inserts one or two cords, and extracts it.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to hot abscess that has come there, then it is not necessary to work at all.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	instead it is necessary to administer wet and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the doctor applies ointments, and uses water-like, softening, and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it equal, then administer what we have said for a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do this, then cut it into pieces and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, administer what we have said for hot abscesses that come into the womb.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding comes from the decorrumens, then it should be put in cold water restricting, and administer other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had a dead child in her womb, then she consulted another doctor on that one, and the other doctor refused to treat the dead child.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her backside and swelled up to the point where it opened, and began with great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, and could not find a way to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied ointment with strong traction, and one bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleansed the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in better shape;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived long thus, and sometimes a little bit of bowel came out.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not written this chapter except because when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, with which we bind books; and to the second turning to the two heads of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the combs should be more subtle than the restrainer, and should be made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the wood should be one and a half palms wide, and the margin of the trees one palm, and long one and a half palms.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two links there should be two joints of the same wood, which are tight in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joints are fitted in the mouth of the joint so that it can be opened when one turns the two combs.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in its appearance, should be made of wood from ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of pincers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two joints at the two heads, just like you see, one palm long and one and a half palms wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the joint open all the way to the instrument, then make the woman sit on one seat, with her feet bent and her legs spread out.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then fit the two joints together in the joint, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just like you have done with pincers evenly, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the joint, until the patient does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted, and their shapes are multiplied; and when the mirrors have been prepared, then the work is faster, and higher for men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, because their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her urine, and then make her pass water in condition, and hold your hands at the mouth and navel.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she passes it for that reason, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take a pot, and make a perforation or cover, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the joint, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put one end of the pot and the other head into the mouth of the joint.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steep until the vapors come inside the joint; then make her pass water, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if she remains after this treatment and is not fully cured, instruct the patient to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or with musk mallow of althea, and then apply it in its natural state.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and seek out the secondine; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the joint does not resist the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved slightly to the right and to the left, and then pulled; if it will come out and dislodge itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the joint is too narrow, we have said the treatment for passing water, and for fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not from all that we have said, then beware that you do not force it at the pulling.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the joint, you tie to the woman's thigh, then anoint her with ointment from four-fold pharmacist.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	so it will set and reset her, and come out fully; but nevertheless, when she has burst forth, a foul smell comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then to do fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have proven that fumigation with cress and dried figs works.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles seeing a cord, and one puts the subtle head in its natural state, and the wide heads above the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be over the coals, and let it steep until it is exhausted, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped by a subtle membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it is necessary for the patient to pierce that membrane at her own door, and not pierce with sharp spatulae, and guard the opening so she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist linen in wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put on a thread of flax, and let it stay for days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this swelling comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that swelling: then be cured, as we have said with the thread of flax.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas which come from under the foundation are nodulation, and grow bigger as they come from below the foundation to go away or in the space of the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	so it has one or more fistulas; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and brings forth moisture white or subtle bowel.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are purulent; and they are known by this that it flows out or is ejected or ventilated when the patient has an emission, and by chance one jumps forth.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the junction of the thigh, and just not to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the purulent fistula at the foundation, and not purulent.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you put your two fingers or foundation, and put a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuousness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, then put on a subtle linen tent or one hair of horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your own touch;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and it doesn't come out through the anus or vomiting or urine, as we have said;
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it will not pass through; so hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced all the way to the bladder or all the way to the urethral conduit, if it urinates and cannot be sealed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced all the way to the junction of the groin, then the tent comes up to its place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the origin of the pain around it, then it is that it will go away in a day or two, and neither medicine nor ointment can help.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these pierced fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and the vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not pierced and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced,
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts his legs up to his groin, and has his groins inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put on a linen tent or one of earth if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then it is fitting that you put your two fingers there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then sense immediately that the tent has pierced it; and be discovered where you feel between your finger and the skin or flesh, then know that it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says however that some can be well healed, but this is rare;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one makes there, it is that one cauterizes the subtle fire according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot in the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those charred parts are burned, which are like the feathers of a bird;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with moist tents in butter, until those charred parts are gone; then treat with ointment anointing the char and closing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, that's good. If not, otherwise it cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters and does not pierce all the way to the skin which is at the fundament, and between your two fingers and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula where the covering of the key ends;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	then cut at the beginning of the fistula, and put it afterwards before the tent, and then apply the cautery after, until it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be delivered the tent, and it will fall; then remove those charred parts that resemble a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine quickly.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cauterizes two main things: namely, the burning of those charred parts joined together, and the stopping of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat with moist tents in butter or in crushed hazelnuts, until the patient's flesh grows well, and the charred parts that were burned go away in the well.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with ointments that harden and dry out tough flesh, and are the drying medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way down to the fundament, and is separated from the body, then put your two fingers on the fundament, and explore that part.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between two is the thread or skin or flesh, where it is about to pierce, then there should be only force that comes from faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can, put tents and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and don't go too deep in the fundament, lest you cut the tenant that holds the fundament, and it will come out by involuntary evacuation.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it afterwards when it is cut near the fundament, by tent or by other instrument appointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove that charred part which is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And no fistulas are according to this manner: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	so take a pierced tent at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one twisted thread in two, and put the tent all around the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If she is pierced in the margin of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that perforation, so that you put your two fingers on the fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw the head of the thread, and tie the two knots together, and strain one against the other, and leave it for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, until the thread cuts through those charred parts that are between two, and fall away.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it's not fitting to make a cut that is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula-like spine from which one makes the fistula is very rough in one place and hollowed out.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, because of which one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	bleedings
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Bleedings are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, like a drop of resin, and there are small and great ones, and it cuts away slowly blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more, and they are without foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are without foundation have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then again or a little bit of yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them inside the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to stretch themselves out in chambers, until the foundations come forth, and they are revealed by children;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	so hasten, and hold it with pincers or at your fingernail, then cut it in its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ligature cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them up on one drapery, or on a cloth, or from a piece of cambric;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them to your hands, then cut, and powder them with some hot powders that are in place of cauterization;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said or written in the chapter of cauterization, then treat with other treatments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purgative him with a biting and sharp purge to wash away what is in the foundation, so that it may come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient is prepared, and if the fibers are gone from the foundation, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that is that you take them at your fingernail or with pincers, and cut, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	and it is necessary that you bring the suture together in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and cause the needle to pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread underneath the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of the length; and tie the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for correcting any superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him be so long as he has a bowel movement, and when they will have ceased, then treat with ointment and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the scorching of the devil or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it happens that scorching of the devil occurs in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is useless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	and it is necessary that you scrape off at the tip of a spatula or at your fingernail the scab above, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat him until he is sound as it befits;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot become sound, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until he is healed and scabbed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is healed.
dou fremit	of the shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Furuncle is a small appearance of abscess above the body, and goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the abscess freezes, and it feels like death from shivering, and comes throughout the body, and more on the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a goose quill or a strong turkey feather, and put that quill on the furuncle, until the circles around it are purple all over.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the whole quill until you cut all around the furuncle, and put it deep in, and extract the furuncle from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is necessary to do so with an iron or steel wire according to this form, and be subtle underneath and drawing upwards.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor pierce, but keep it at the point of your finger, and press hard And if you see that, then cauterize the furuncle, as is written or described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the purge
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purge of silver or archaut, or melted iron or cloth; and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments, according to how they are prepared for use.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are prepared for the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the purge, whether small or great, is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and if there is a deviation or the belly is bound, as you see, and the fibers are pierced within; and has on one side two perforations, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and if the belly or womb is opened, put in medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small perforations.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have between each perforation one thread of esparto, then put in these perforations a strong thread twisted from coarse thread, either ten or twenty times around, and sew up the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then purge; and that is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and the medicine not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the purge with oil or egg white or something similar, then tie it loosely.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then instruct the attendants to hold it with their two hands together, until it is fully opened, then pull out the purge, and lift up the patient's legs to the appearance.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then tie it tightly as much as you can; and if he sleeps a whole night afterwards, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge him in a disease of gut obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, then the purge should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the form of the subtle purge on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the section on wounds: now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where they are made, and according to how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or with a lance or club or spear, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	wherever they are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head, simple ones, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from falling onto stone or similar things, and although the skin is torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you slightly doubt the abscess being hot: if you make it heal quickly, from the same head, even if it comes out with blood from the wound, and the healing is contrary to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to be filled with wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not wish to heal, then let his meat be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place it on the wound, if a hot abscess comes forth, with wet cotton in rose oil alone, or in vinegar.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air or powder, which I will say a little further.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the abscess has been moved, then place on some ointments, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together with suturing, just as I will say for wounds of the belly, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to bone and bleeding, and holds together by only a little bit, then cut it open; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked testicles and wheat, as well as fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a purulence on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut out the whole purulence, and let blood flow, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped with medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it severed, tie it up with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put in this powder which hardens even when the abscess has been moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and pound it subtly,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill the wound, and bind it firmly, until it closes well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and let it be without loosening, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one does this only with coal alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but only when the abscess has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the abscess has moved the wound, and it is in this state, then do not put any of this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but place on some digestive ointments or poultices made from wheat flour and water mixed with honey, until it discharges pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the breakage of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you afterwards about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and put nothing restraining, for it hurts the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but be the medicine soothing, such as coal washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and also wash the cloth in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of my kind according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and are filled with pus and blood, then pierce or open them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes forth, then dissect it, tie it up, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut or the cords are severed, and the conduit is preserved, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew the cord on the gasket of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it gently, and let it be for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until he is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cut it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave what you cannot until the wound has purged.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be severed and ligated the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a wound from a lance or dagger, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are symptoms that the patient will not recover: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't put powder in at the first hour, nor bind it tightly because the blood would not have a chance to pour out deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and revive in the heart, and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have oil, put old cotton in the wound to suck up moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep over the wound three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no convulsion, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor any sign of lunacy;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with tents and other treatments until he is well.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal or work, then know that there is a fistula; and cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, on the front or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is pressed into the bone, and has split into pieces, then close the wound, and remove the flesh if it is separated.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, then let the wound dry out, so that it will ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, middling, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound some times the intestines or the membranes of the intestines burst, whereby their introduction occurs;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the great one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore one should put the intestines back in gradually, rather than all at once.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they enter more slowly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore the middle wound is worse, because one must reposition the intestine to its place, which takes longer than two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and a greased thing is for putting back, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen from cold.
