Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one cloth of linen in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you heat the water with warm things like aquant, cypress, and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and then reposition the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine restrains and is more effective at deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or heat that has been cooked with ale and malt.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this it is eased the entry of some things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is more effective than the cutting.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	than none should cut without great necessity being there;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside in the curvature and do not take out anything, but look at the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine protrudes further,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in accordance with its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because this is more effective.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part under the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part under the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so place the head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so place your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to follow what I say about great and middle-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Put small wounds in the treatment that appears good to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take into your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound one or two fingers' width, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two joints of the skin with the two joints of the siphac.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that side,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the siphac into three;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a doubled thread around the needle in two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and bring together the two edges of the wound naturally,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one or two fingers' width, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do so according to how many needles you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles of medium size, between fine and coarse.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the very fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound before the stitches.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient while he is sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the ends of the needles to hold them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is closed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one or two needles suffice.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you tie the two skin stitches and the two skin stitches together with a needle that has one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these pieces three together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then tie the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitching the thickness of a minor denier;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is suitable for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that one man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width deep.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it exposed the intestines well two palms' width deep,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine and it had been outside for 24 hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed in just 15 days, and I cured it, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I didn't cure him with ointment, because I was in one place where you couldn't find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put a cloth with old cotton on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it through to the inside from the outer part, just up to that point;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the flesh in a straight line, then tie the end of the skin or costet to where you inserted the needle;
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inner part up to that point outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as peltiers do with furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the skin once on one side and then take it up again on the other, until the stitching is all complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galen calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like what some people do, who join the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the skin to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or chief of the mirror near, and make it pierce only that point;
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two skin stitches;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part up to that point inside;
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	like two skin stitches;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part up to that point inside, in two other skin stitches that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says this phrase, and some testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew leather;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is a stitching more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as that of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it's that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and the air has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the skin; then place on top a powder of burnt charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the air has changed it, then put on some ointment that is available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and tie together the skin and the flesh;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you do with others, until it is well.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it two times a day until he is well.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in many simple wound situations;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound may cause community of members to principal parts,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it's good for you to moisten linen lightly with oil of temperate heat or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the angles and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or torment in his bowels, and this often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse him with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the torment comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and make an incision inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal if it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is due to the plantiness of veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of all the body, and the approaching nature of its humors.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts forth from the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, as long as it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, then it's good that you stop the flow of blood from coming out.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then tie what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two stitches hanging from the part below the wound up to the outside to ease the extraction when the intestines fall out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is rent, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from there came the evacuation and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I knew how, and did not cease to subtlety until he was well and the flesh was joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no evil, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experts say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh figs from great testicles, then bind the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the fig has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then bind the head tightly, so that it cannot come loose.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another fig behind in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This remedy works well in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread taken from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that is quite clean-shaven,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread one thin twisted linen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then push the thread through the needle and sew up the intestine, and then tie it in a knot;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing with figs is nothing other than according to the way of hope and expectation;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the intestinal grooves, there is no remedy or health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that all wound or abscess, when it suppurates, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it bursts and runs pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to the true nodulation, hard and white, or where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it bursts forth like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it runs clear pus, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing other than through one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside and above the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the humors are corrupted, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in the region, digestion is slow and health is delayed, and is naturally inflamed;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I make you aware of the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the kidney, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar humors.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of great suffering, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the level I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it and know it, take a piece of iron or lead, if the fistula is straight, then pierce it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle instrument of steel.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the steel bends with ease around the twistiness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by instruments,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings;
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture thus runs from one opening to another and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then pierce with all your might, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and it bursts forth in the very depth.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels as you apply pressure with your hand, and the location where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the locations I have told you, then bind it according to what I have said;
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the bad humors and corrupted flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well opened from its proper place, then it is necessary that you open it further, as far as you can;
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put in moistened instruments of medicine, and tie them just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put in ointments and unguents of healthy flesh, until it is cleansed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not cleansed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then bind it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves are not injured or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it all until the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with things of unguent flesh until it is cleansed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not cleansed and bursts forth again as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet arrived at the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	uncover and pierce until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus cleansed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep in the bottom, and you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature's will.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can remove it with pincers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many of them, treat all together, leaving none.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	so mix and moisten and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you can't remove them in an hour, place on the wound something that will cause rotting.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it stay until the flesh is rotten around the bones.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have come loose from the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a great bone, such as one of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	so remove only the corrupt part until all the flesh is gone.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there's a great part of the corrupt flesh and it comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so scrape and char everything up to the corruption, and then cure until it is bound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg and became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to delay opening it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the barber, through his foolishness, cut too deeply so that the abscess opened.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great deal of matter was flowing out, and it became a fistula, and there came many pus-filled boils that all flowed forth with foul discharge from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many barbers treated it for about two years, and there was no improvement in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medications with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed out through the boils was great in amount.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young man turned red and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a tent into one of those boils, and then searched out all the boils.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some were connected to others on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then and charred one of the boils until I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming right down to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared from the rotten bone and thought that there was no other corruption except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medications over a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I repeated the process, and discovered the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then extracted it, and thought to set the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I charred around a palm of bone, and brought it to its very edge.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medications; and it was healed and set quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to repeat the work except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the bloodletting it often bled out, but he was healed completely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone a hard callus arose, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or obstacle from anywhere, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be scraped out in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one thread and strain it to the top of the open bone.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another thread of linen a bit thicker than the first one, and tie it on top of the flesh that is above the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top so that you pull the rotten flesh downwards.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the bone on the spot where you see it needs to be scraped, so that the scraper does not harm the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot iron or a piece of wood below the bone in order to heat up and dry out the rotten flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and scrape again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is rotten, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it.
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron below,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one part to the other the rotten flesh, and make sure the scraper is as long as the length of the corruption, just as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then char the rotten joint, and scrape the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to char it.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the armpit of the hand or in the armpit of the foot, then that thing is very strong.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary for you to inquire into that corrosion, how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve be contrary to you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and scrapers for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument you need according to what it requires.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder can become dislocated due to a cause from within or due to a cause from without.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried medicinal treatment for that corrosion, and it does not bring any benefit,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut that member down to the point where the corruption comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes either by death or by malice, which is greater, due to the default of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are such that the member becomes black, so that it seems as though it has been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then after the darkness, then goes forth the corrosion of member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes throughout the body; if you hasten to cover.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the joint, if he copes, and does not give him any space to come all the way to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes all the way to the hand, then he copes at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come all the way to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then he copes at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that's death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so it does when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then he copes after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then he copes all the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the leg, then he copes at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of binding or wrapping the member is that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister downwards with one band, and another minister upwards with the other band.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you separate the flesh that is between the two bands to one and a half spatula-widths wide, so that the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then he binds or wraps it, and places one linen cloth on each side, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess arise in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put some restraining powders on top; then return to your medicine until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in summer fever:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a darkness that seemed like the burning of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to his foot's joint, so that it spread throughout all his foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to bind up his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards, the corruption returned to the joint of his hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that would cause a reaction after the purification of the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said I should cut off his hand, and I did not agree, for I had hope of causing the matter to recede.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the man's virtues were weak; and he became desperate altogether, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to bind up his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I told this story only because it is necessary to make other amends when needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At times an abscess forms in the fatty part of the skin, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and opens, and the pus jumps out, and the skin remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as subtle as one of those delicate drapery fabrics.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach all the way to the bone, nor all the way to the nerve, and such diseases are called "st. Augustine's".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes all the way to the bone in front, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is like this: you wrap that skin all around, and even when it is subtle, just like a fabric.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not harden because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you think the skin will harden, and the corruption is not in front.
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thickened with flesh, so cure it with ointment thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are large, and the pus that flows from them has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then use Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aiseal, and oil, and lye, in equal parts, and put the mixture into one vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use the medicine to lubricate the breast, and stop the abscess.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in place for two hours, then remove it by dripping.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed.

quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ash from the vine's firewood, and pour water on top.

et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess on the breast is small, and the tube of the lubricant cannot enter it,

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the boil is deep, do not allow raw flesh to remain.

car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the boil is deep, do not allow raw flesh to remain.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut under the skin as you see

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elbow
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Fleabite is an abscess that grows under the elbow of the armpit of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or by chance occurs in other joints;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not looked after, then a foul abscess comes.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and drains pus until it reaches the root of the elbow, and by chance may even drain all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to the corrosion just to the bone, so that it brings a stinking pain, and the joint of the joint is wide, and the color is flux.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you cut away all the excess flesh that remains from the elbow.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the elbow joint is intact;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint begins to fester and start to prick and bleed.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so it is necessary that you put a cloth under the elbow where the flesh is pricking.

puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with oils until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and treat further, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the joint corroding, then cut it out in one piece just as it is said before.

et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The joints that occur in some people's hands by chance are all fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is such a joint where it has bones, and sometimes it has no elbow.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the joints of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that occurs in any part of the finger does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and the one that occurs at the joint of the finger, by chance, moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one that occurs in the root of the joint is hard to cure: if you are hesitant to cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In he who is born or will die soon, it is necessary that you cut first the skin around just to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone to a suitable thread for him, then cure until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come together must be gathered from birth, or from a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.

puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or moistened cloths dipped in rose oil, so that they do not stick together.

Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are swollen large and puffed out, full of superfluous melancholic things, that come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it is more common in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer to him sometimes purging of bile, and then the medicine of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is according to two manners: one is when you cut them, and then treat the black blood that flows out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein, and let all the blood flow.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: first arise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood becomes thinned.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a broad incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and let flow the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood has flowed out as the patient can bear.

Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The removal of the abscess is according to this manner: rise the patient's leg, if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and rise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell.

et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot treat and lift it, then insert an awl into every strong thread doubled.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and treat it, and insert below one thread, and turn your hand from side to side until it flows out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and take care that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot treat or lift it, and it comes to harm the patient.

si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it twistedly, but do not cut it off; and treat it just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron with which you cut the vein is curved, and does not cut straight, so that it cuts the vein.

De la voinne civile	Note: It seems like you've provided only "De la voinne civile" which is likely a mistake. The original text was divided into lines, and this line seems to be missing some part of the sentence. Please provide the complete sentence if possible.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is engendered in legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs nor trees, and in land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the impurity that comes from below the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if it came from within the body as a serpent or a worm, engendered between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the swelling changes and the vein begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens up, then it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two and a half inches, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it becomes undone, wrap it around the cloth again, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut off its root until it has come out entirely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and impurity in that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that it be treated gradually up to the top, and leave none of it in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is when it is treated for five or ten palms in length,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it was that issued from ten palms in length, and when you cut it, he inserted a thread or a pipe, and pierced it down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that everything be; and let the matter inside be empty, and bring to place medicines that can prevent any harm for a year, then care for it as if it were an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at no time to this vein many streams, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot or the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes out much pus, and from which many streams come forth; then cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "bovine sickness", because it often afflicts oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down through the entire body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it is felt well from one member to another, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and bursts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the corruption of some humors, such as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids or those in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt is had about its wickedness, for when it goes through the body and climbs to the head and comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and pulled out, one can't avoid but when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then you must tie the place above and below with a strong band tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and pull it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you can't find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it destroys the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then hold a strong band below it, then cut above and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient with purging of the body's medicines which dissolve bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of meat that can prevent harm.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vacirir", and is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then spreads from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rising like a worm on the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, like vivid silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while after it ran through the entire body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was twisting around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had heard of many that had indeed experienced pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it myself, just as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that this was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore this windiness appeared constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason for those who are luxurious, and who have moist bodies and veins that are closed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then tie above and below quickly, and then cut above until that constrained windiness bursts forth.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you don't see it to your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with what hinders windiness, such as fetid pills and serpent's pill, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are some with large points, and small ones, and those with barbs, and those with shafts;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two angles, and of those that have tongues, and of those that are broken into pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which strikes some member does so in two ways: either it enters the principal member, or it breaks off;
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes then in some place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary to beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many dispositions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the skull bursts forth which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is blindness and madness and bewilderment and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is without further breath from the nostrils, or the ears; and by chance perturbs speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and bursts forth with a moist white wound resembling boils, and bursts out like a stream of flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the cure, and pull out the arrow if it's not stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow becomes still like boils, and flows with black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when the kidney is hit is that without any foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's color changes, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the breastbone, it is near the little ribs; and vomits a great deal of yellow bile and great pain and sighs; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow strikes the stomach by chance, so that something from the undigested meat falls out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow strikes the belly, and a piece of bowstring jumps out through the intestines without any hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes the bladder, and urine jumps out and flows forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and shoulders and throat and shoulder blade and armrest and spine of the back and forehead and hips and thighs and legs, and a similar limb, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to me once when an arrow struck the shoulder in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I drew out an arrow that struck in the fatty part of the eye under the paper-thin skin,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and I could not pull it out except for a small portion towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, very light without iron tips; the wound was healed, and no bad accident occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with iron tips:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loosened the barbs, and pulled it out slowly until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from a man who had been struck in the belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed 30 days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out further, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has been struck by an arrow on the back, and the wound is sealed above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did he find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man who has been struck by an arrow on his face, and the wound is sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from the king of the princes, who had been struck near the nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly bent to the right side; and the arrow was completely stuck.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for the treatment after it had been struck three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with a very fine touch, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the wound a plaster that attracts and digests, because the flesh did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the arrow's point appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster for many days, and the wound was resolved above, and remained thus the patient a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound medicinal corrosive mixture for many days, until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to remove it, and felt the head of the arrow which was stuck at the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted it into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed well beyond the term for 3 months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then it sloughed off so much that I inserted the forceps, and pulled at it from one side and the other, but it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to search and extract it by means of instruments, until I took hold of it one day with the well-made forceps,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot entirely comprehend;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can grasp something very small, and that which is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	nine works, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit from the limbs where they are stuck except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the way they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out from where it enters is an arrow entering flesh and jumping out at times.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, then let it remain until the flesh is pierced around, and the exit is opened.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, then let it remain like that for some days, and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it doesn't, then pierce around with a very fine point, until the flesh around is stretched out, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just up to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said come to the patient: then do not pull it out at all, but let it remain equal after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the sacral bone, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come up to the sacral bone,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains the patient for some days without bad accident, then pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out further, then administer theriacs around, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in its place within the body so that it cannot be seen, then it seeks out the entire tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut so that the wound will be large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow as to why it stays there,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so remove the flesh that is stuck between two parts of the wound as far as you can;
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the next day and pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and put in place how you can draw out the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
