Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, or if it touches anything of his, or the skin is swollen in front where one can see or feel something abnormal;
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then on top, as far as the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, as far as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes forth;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck, then push it through to the whole length;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head breaks off, and you wish to administer a poultice, then apply one instrument with a cloth;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the cloth of the instrument; and then push forth;
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is broken, then apply one instrument with a pointed end into it, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow breaks or splits open in the back, belly, bladder, or side, and it is nearby, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then cut the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and petty, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the cloth-bound instrument is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as shown by this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for extracting is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins by which one is healed there are 31, of which 16 are in the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two jugular veins that are located after the ears, which are called "herbech" in pairs;
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspirés";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lip above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins by which one is healed commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the arm, and people commonly call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people commonly call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people commonly call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that by which one is healed, which appears manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena vein is the one that is between the ulnar and radial veins, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the fold of the armpit on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphena which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nese", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of the veins that are after the ears helps the ancient catharrics and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the skin or veins with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then comes to your hand, and where you feel the pulse below your hand, if it signals by pulling;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand above the entire vein;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and the vein well for two hands of traverse, and make the blood come out as far as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and bind it, so that it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The vein of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth to migrate anciently,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and when sore and obtalmic, accustomed to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the blood are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below the tongue, and then signs off;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key above the vein at the top of the tongue's index, and put the lancet below;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein above, and cut it, just as you did with the two other veins, and make the incision of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your tongue on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face, and to migrate and to blush;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting, so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the point on the vein, and press with your hand or other thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed, and never once to open a wide opening.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the opening be too wide; and the wound to cross, because the bone is pressed, and by chance break the opening when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The vein of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts is helpful to the eyes, and to the typhoid fever, and to the blush, and to the jaundice in the eye, and to diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their vein are such that the patient stretches his neck while twisting without any bond, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it be, and be the vein of the traverse, about a little bit long and a little bit wide, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the opening is subtle, by chance it will break; then make an incision of blood, until you have need of it, and then bind on cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the navel is worth to evacuate, and to unblock, and to diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	just as migraine and blush that comes in the face, and similarly when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient stretches his neck, then strains his navel to your left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle and long opening, and insert it between the two nostrils in the space that is between the two naris;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep in, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it is very soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the opening:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The vein of the two groins is helpful to the obstruction of the womb, and to the beginning of menstruation, and to many diseases, and to constipation, and to corrosion, and to herpes, and to ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient stretches his neck below one and the other, just as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit down on one seat;
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then let out the vein of the long opening a little bit widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other side in the other vein, then release the ligament, and bind the veins moderately;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	The vein of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the upper lips is helpful to purging in the mouth, and to corrupting of gums, and breaking of lips, and around the navel.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	and the qualities of the vein are such that make the patient sit down before you, and strain his neck just as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one on each side, and similarly make of the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	The vein under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein under the tongue is helpful after the cephalic vein, and it is for the obstruction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks under each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then cut one and the other, and do not go too deep in, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck which we commonly bleed are veins that are bled according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or in piercing a wide and deep opening, or an olive-like subtle one as cutlers cut, and is called "anasil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the wideness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the wide opening is well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are filled with thick blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-like opening:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, or where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the Basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is helpful for diseases that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the breast, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	It is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him slightly, and beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a lot of blood comes out, then it is necessary to stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be pinched with the flame, but cut like ash.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open obviously, then it is necessary to remove it, and change another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want any part of it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the arm: it opens obviously;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the flame like ash, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you remove the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulsation;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a marker, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the flame like ash;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: stop then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flow upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is the artery's blood;
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your finger above for a long time, then take away your finger if the blood ceases, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be above fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not ceased, and it complains to you, and the remedy is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retires; and cease the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a wrapping of fustic, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it well up to the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the blood is ceased, it's good; if not, then cure him, as we have said, with powders that cease blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the ceasing is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the power of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein of the blood in the middle so helps that it takes away blood from the head above and from the belly below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is below, and if it points too deep inside, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the patient's health is grievous, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you loosen the nerves with the instrument like ash; and stop the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is vein between the two nerves, then cut the long piece.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the cephalic so helps that it takes away blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed slightly with the olive flame or with the myrrh flame, for it is the most safe of all the veins, for it does not have below the nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek out the lighter place, and do not hurt anything if one should fail the first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance some people's places swell up, so that one may fail the first time, but it does not hurt anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not done for anything else but to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent illnesses from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are used: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of pentecosts to clean, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after 2 hours or 3 of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no fixed determination, but when there is need by day or night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying more than the fourth month up to the seventh;
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one bleed elderly people who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, then it is necessary that they purge the intestines with a light clyster;
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not take away from the intestines the superfluities which are hurtful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one bleed one who is too fat from meats, nor one who is drunk, until they are sober and free from dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of bleeding after a passion of the colon, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequent coitus with women, and travail, watching, and sleeping, and all that pertains to the virtue, or by something of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then put him in a bath, unless something prevents it, to subtlety the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein of the bladder around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from work, and toil, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be lazy and joyful, and let the bleeding be higher than that person to whom one is bleeding, and rub the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then remove the bandage gradually, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood will not flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell up, and one can feel it;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bleeding area with the flame of an old oil, then put your thumb on your left hand on that vein below the place where you want to bleed,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not flee and fail at the moment of bleeding.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings when one is bleeding, and some that are full of windiness;
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so when one applies the caustic, it takes back to itself and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the surgeons be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first time, that is good; if not, then it starts again a little below or above quickly, as long as the swelling is not present.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is present and the patient is frightened, then leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	by chance an abscess will form; do not enter into a bath, then begin the treatment again if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the wound is not bleeding subtly and you doubt that it will not bleed so much as you see, then trust in that same opening to all the fire directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little quickly, so long as the swelling is present; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the swelling, then do not begin the treatment again, and apply a little bit of oil, for it lightens the body from blood, and is helpful in this swelling to bind that which the oil binds;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil binding in each treatment of veins that you heal the wounds, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done for a triangle and a bowl of eyes, when it is applied to the swelling; then subtly the blood flows out and spreads when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a big abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not treated except at that time or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten and apply a moist sponge to the swelling in water and silk, and bind it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the swelling for several days with no blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, apply something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in camel's milk, mixture, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica; then place your hand on it, and if you find the swelling soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything of what we have said, for by chance it may cause constriction of the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the swelling, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to make the wound larger, and let the caustics be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and have him heal little by little, and it is necessary to have him heal by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from hemorrhage and numbness of the nerve, and is worth more than the healing of the long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body is failing at the wound, it is necessary to give wet bread in the juice of ripe pomegranates; if he is overheated, then treat with bloodletting three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, then moisten the bread before the wound with a sweet syrup, or with an aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cresses, and a well-odored syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he belches at the wound, after the flow of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks a broth of bone and a subtle, well-odored syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bend his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bend his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he heals in seven hours after the first bleeding, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another side, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body that is already overheated and makes one come down with a fever; then it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until it becomes a pomegranate.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you reward all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on the pulse when it is healing, so that death may not come instead of a pomegranate.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see that the arm should be loosened, and blood let out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless it is curved, then he should straighten his arm quickly, for it would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him heal the second time; or you should put it at the tip of the caustic, until the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein flows freely,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and apply a little bit of silk soaked in water, and press lightly upon.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires bleeding a second time, then let the blood flow in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are healed at the place of the main vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the scab becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is bound gently so that the veins appear well, then he heals now across, not long or wide.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the opening is wide, and heals well near the joint of the hand, and if there is no more blood to come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if this is in summer, do not throw the hand into hot water, for it is put more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vine is saved from all other veins, since it has no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the right arm is worth to all liver diseases, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is emptied, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein crosses over, and you take it all out in one, then nothing troubles it;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep into the flesh, for the nerves are beneath all the stripped away flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if the wound is frozen in the incision, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as needed, put oil and silk on the vein to cauterize quickly, and thus do for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is worth to the disease of the mouse, and do the same as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The vein of the Sophen is worth to all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of urine, and disease of the reins, and groins, and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this vein is that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it breaks.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lies above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many rains go.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then it is good for the larger rain or the one at the ankle that is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you make it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and the vein should go across as in cutting; and let there be no inflammation.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot back in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding fails at first, then repeat it a second time above by a little, for the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and do likewise with the Sophen of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the thigh, and its vein is worth for the pain in the hip when it is full of blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this vein is that the patient goes in or out of a bath and stretches above the ankle four fingers by twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then cause it to bleed in all ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth more than you can cut it, for the flesh is sound, and it is very responsive to many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then cause some other vein to open on the back of the foot or towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and cause as much blood to flow as you see, and then loosen the ligament, and put cotton on it and restrain it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	(The phrase "Des sainies de ventouse" appears to be a section header or title, indicating that the following text will discuss the subject of wound dressings using cupping glass)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by making an incision and drawing blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that is done without making an incision is in two ways: either it is done with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping that is done by making an incision and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	one being all on the top of the head, and the others in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck; and the cupping below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping on both shoulders; and the cupping above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cuppings in both arms; and the cuppings in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cuppings of the two ankles; and the cupping does not treat blood, unless it is from small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one should not be afraid of it, just as one would with a vein dressing;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, whether with fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to cup due to the severity of diseases or for habit, then we should administer it each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to cup, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find repletion and darkness in their face, and head, and neck, and in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have the tongue swollen, and bleed freely;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to cup after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The vein of the Muse helps with the headache that comes to one's eyes, and it is not necessary for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this cupping is in place of the vein of the Cephalic.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not necessary for someone with a cold complexion or who has chattering (probably referring to St. Vitus' dance) to do this, as it would cause them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly or those with cold diseases of the head to use this treatment.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often cured with this method will become forgetful, and because of this it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping on the neck is in place of the vein of the head and Basilica, and because of this it is worth for the constriction of the belly.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to splitting of the channel of the womb, and all over, and to repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to apply a little pressure, for if it holds too tightly, it will cause forgetfulness or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The hiccoughs with the two ribs of the neck if they are worth the pains of the head, and obtalmic eye and migraine, and in strangulation, and in pain to the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the saintly basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the surgeon to express his hand when he puts it, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not bring forth copious blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The hiccoughs under the chin if they are worth a disease of the mouth, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the cures of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The hiccoughs of the shoulders are worth a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The hiccoughs of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it brings forth blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deep for fear, because the flesh is bare of fat, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The hemorrhoids that are on the backside are worth hemorrhoids of the fundament, and diseases below, and it is necessary that the hemorrhoid be large, and be of earth, so it has need to well draw out; and by chance, if they were subtle, they would break; and there would be great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The hemorrhoids of the legs are clearly healed, for they bring forth blood from all the body, and are worth the ancient pains of the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and restore the flowers; and they are in the place of the two shins, and two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause to come forth pus in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the poultice is that you put it on first empty, and then succeed in a timely way, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do so until you see the place red and swollen, and behold the bleeding of blood; then cut, and remove the poultices, and take heed to the condition of the body, for there are some who have hard flesh, and clear pores: thus it is necessary to wound only once, and necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then it is necessary to wound twice: the first time to subtlety the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to wound a third time; and when we wish to draw out the blood little by little, then we should be satisfied only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to draw out a lot of blood, then we often recommence; and if the blood is thick, then cut deeply, and finish so that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for him who has thick skin and hard flesh, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the poultices with oil that is appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed of gourd oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's in winter, with oil of wormseed, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one who is being cured has tender flesh and large pores, there's no need to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should wash with ease, or with myrtle water, and sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should wash with old wine, or with water of sycamore, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to wash with a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep at all after the application.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he washes, when he should be poulticed and when he is being poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is being cured is choleric, and the blood is too abundant and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	and it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green grapes and endive and lettuce in ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and then take a little, and meat of castrated animals, and moist flesh.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine that is midway between old and new, and eat little by little, and eat small birds and young pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be poulticed, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give certain people at times treacle or muscat before the poulticing, or afterwards, to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be subtlety drawn out, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The poultices that are applied without wounding are those that are applied on the liver, and on the kidneys, and podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the loin, for these members do not suffer to be wounded in this way.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only so that blood can be drawn out from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we apply to the mammary glands when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the belly and navel to diminish the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes the pain when there is inflammation or piercing; and by its attractive virtue it may attract the inflammation, or dislodge the piercing from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one applies it to the liver and kidneys when there is retained poultice-like substance.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these poultices are administered empty to suck for as long as only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the pustules, and in this manner one fills the poultice with hot water alone, or with water that has cooked herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered at fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be half a palm wide and one-quarter of an inch thick, and have a rounded edge all around the periphery, just like for inserting a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of earth, soft beforehand so that it does not harm the patient when putting on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in medium a cross-shaped piece of earth or iron to put a candle in hold.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be great and small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for children's poultices are different from old people's, and lean ones' from fat ones'.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this poultice thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or one lining, and put it in the poultice across the piece that is inside the poultice.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and it should be on the boil that we have said, so that when one wants to, if there is steam, and remove the poultice;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining again just like before, and continue it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the poultice then which is administered in illness of pleurisy, it has no cross or boil, and is not administered at all except when it is full of water, and is put on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	and that's the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Poultices are not administered at all except in limbs where one cannot put poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare bones without flesh, such as arms or legs, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find poultices that are in pure and clear water without any putridity, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in sweet water until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be washed with wine and poultice, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and bursting, if it's a place where one can put poultices, then put them, because this is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then take away the bone with ease and then with water, very well, and then bind it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bone heals too late after the poultices' removal, then soak one cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until the poultice is shriveled.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bone is multiplied, then put on vitriol pounded or gallstones and similar things, until it is shriveled.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the bone half of peeled broad beans and leave them until they are absorbed by the bone, so it will dry now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the poultices do not want to take, then rub the bone with fresh blood, or put a needle in it until the pus comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will absorb;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are flowing, then powder on a little bit of alum and powdered silk or ashes, so they will dry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins here.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for fracture and desolation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Learn, dear son, that the foolish man will fall into this chapter, for he has never seen any of the old books nor read a letter;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is the art estranged in our land, for I never found any good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing except by the science of the old books, or that which I have studied and treated, and through experience, and through the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are administered, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is then necessary that we say the prologue to this book, the summary of the word and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or distortion comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one side and the other, unless something else entirely, such as weakness of the body, or children, or old men.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is not very cold or too hot; and moderate choleric heats, that is to say, cold flushes, and flesh of hare and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill with meat which fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot abscess or expansion of matter in the member; then restore the patient to his former government as he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or have viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and testes, and peas, and beef's belly, and eel, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the bones mend more quickly and sooner the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well reunited or mended according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but don't care, reset on the broken bone a big splint that sets and joins the member together, until it becomes strong as before; and do not give up from his work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish him with thick meats, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is one thing and the fracture of the back or leg another, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur when an arrow hits, and another when something is sharpened, like the cutting edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And then there is a fracture with wound, and a fracture in a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own device, and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes into place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breaking of the bone occurs because the joint is twisted, and it becomes clear by the absence, and sounds under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting nor touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no breaking;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But you must not move by hand, but put on the medications that come afterwards, and then restrain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breakage that occurs in arvol, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary to set them now in equal point, so that abscesses do not come alive.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses hot come forth, then let it be left alone for a day, until the abscess is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set it in equal to the mold that you can do lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is more light than the restorations of those who have fragments; then restrain it, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and they are stretched by two parts, whether it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is small members, or by two strings, or by one string and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are dislocated, then reunite by all means the additions in their places to the mold that you can, and take care that through your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And make it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well: then shape it nicely and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who bring forth abscesses hot and contractions in the member, as we have often experienced.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, then chastise the patient well that it does not move, nor in sleeping or waking, nor in turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not yet at the right point, and it is necessary to put it in such a condition that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it be set correctly, lest twisting come there when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: so it is necessary to envelop them in soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are great, such as thighs and leg: so it is necessary to envelop them in a broad and strong linen, for the broad linens embrace all the great member and restrain it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap it around with light bandages, three or four turns depending on the member, and hold your hand lightly to the whole bandage, then go above the break and restrain it less, so that the break may recede a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and make the bandage slightly soft and soft, until you take a great part of the healthy place, then take another bandage and wrap it around again above the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, not too strongly nor too softly, as we have said in the first lesson above.
