puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages pieces of linen or cloths, until it is all even, then tie everything above with one gauze, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something calming the hot abscess, and which takes away the swelling, and let it be like that for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then restrain on your splints, and be of the middle part of a well-seasoned cane, or of elm wood from which one makes cleats, or of palm reeds, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the break be a little bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it needs to be for the small or great member.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then restrain on the splints as you did in the first lesson, then tie above with a thread smoothly, just as in the first lesson above the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the more it is tight above, the less below; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bands with twisted linen cords, and that's a great error, because the band cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that there should be less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the splints' edges after the restraining in the healthy places, then put below them bandages of linen or woolen cloth, so that it does not get cut.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the skin is torn, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to restrain all broken members with splints on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are great, it is not necessary to put splints on them except after five or seven days, or more according to your security regarding hot abscesses that may occur;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore breaks, dislocations, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that remains by the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great deal of egg, and put this concoction, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and that's the common manner of the plaster restoring the break in various ways, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twisting: take aloes, ladani, and asphodel, and gum arabic, and mugwort, each 10 times; myrrh and aloe, each 5 times; and alchemil 8 times; and grind into powder, and mix with a great deal of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to embalm that is good for twisting: take mugwort and wormwood, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 8 parts; acaica, 5 parts; Armenian balm, 10 parts, and crush well, and mix with vinegar or abundance of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way to embalm for joints and bones that have separated from their places, and soothes the pain occurring, and the usage of the bone and the breaking: take fresh linen, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place. These emplasters do not restore at all, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly taking away pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to embalm that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and leaves of earthy parsley, and crush them together, and make an emplaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way to embalm for the restoration of bone breaking and to soften the remaining abscess. Take root of wormwood, camomile, violet flowers, and vetch flour, each one part; and crush, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way to embalm even stronger than the first one, when abscesses that are hard to come back to the restoration of the member. Take roots of wormwood, and flax seeds, balauston, mellilot, and sansho, and violet and camomile flowers, each one part; and crush, and mix with salt water or sweet water or with wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it with anything other than a wax and oil mixture, and nothing more, and he says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it with dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to embalm that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort and horse's mane, or bird feathers, and wormwood, in equal parts, and crush them, and make an emplaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone returned to its place; if not, do not loosen for four days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the emplaster now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and plunge into water, and lift up the place until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a nut, until you are sure of hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and be taken away the pain, then recommence the gentle binding, and a little emplaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and bind subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling are all gone, and you need to apply an emplaster and binding, then begin again, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, then do not loosen it for more than three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes let it rest twenty days, according to what is seen, until the breakage is settled, and approaches the joining of the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then apply the restraint more than initially, and let the swelling decrease in meat, just as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that no nourishment can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	And then arise the liquid with hot water each time you loosen it, and let it be every third day, and ease off a little bit on the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, then, cut off the nourishment to the member, and hasten to do what foolish surgeons do, who leave the member twisted: that is bad, and it is a woeful occupation, and I see nothing else but languishing and working improperly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breakages, and various shapes, and the causes are determined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breakages that are caused by the percussion of a sword, and the collar bone is broken, with all the bone up to the socket which is below the bone, as if struck by a hammer or mallet; and because of this it is called "hauching" or "hammering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing, and it is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound from these two breakings can be great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a thrusting blow, or a split or breakage of the collarbone, or falling on stone, or from jumping down steps, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a breaking that presses, which approaches just to the skin that is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound can be great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is opened in the bone as thin as a hair, and it is a small split, and because of this it is called this breaking "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made or caused by hitting with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the bone piece go down, and it looks like what blacksmiths do when they hammer on the furnaces; so the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And these things happen more often to those who have or have had moist skulls, like those of children.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and these things happen in all these ways of breaking, where small pieces are separated like that; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breaking by subtraction on them, and inquiry at the tests, and through the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and strokes it with a cloth above, then the black breakage appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the breakage, take care to note the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, extension, paralysis, fever, and the like coming out and reddening, and other similar things in more or less disposition, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unforeseen accident, and you expect salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when wounds come to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day from the time you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, lest the flesh beneath the bone be corrupted, and come the accidents that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break in the bone comes just to the flesh that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut the broken part thus: and that you take hold of the patient's head, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound as gently as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the flow of blood comes to reveal the bone, or an abscess appears, then apply the remedy that is needed, and it is that you fill the place with moistened cloths in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done in two ways of work: one manner is that you cut the removal narrow beforehand, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put one other cutting larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse cuttings, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron sharp; and work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, then it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuttings with tarers, not too deep lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and it should have above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place in the shape of the bone, so that you have tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one tare above the bone, and turn it to your two sides until you know the bone is pierced; then place the tare elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut out the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertu, and make it as subtle as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sacral vertebra.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and trimmed, then it is necessary that you reset the apposition that remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it should be more taut and more subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, then remove them lightly with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with poultices and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Gauls say, which is more sure; and it is very strong, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this incisor-like instrument, and this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and this is the part that is aged in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you cut lightly around the bone, and take good care of the flesh that is beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then remove it lightly, for one removes it without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the flesh, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to remove the scales with a subtle scraper of which you should have various quantities, so as to apply the most suitable remedy in each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So scrape first with great scrapers, and then with more subtle ones, and do not stop until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuttings and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you apply remedy according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily grasped by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sacrum is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not wound the sacrum, then administer above one layer of linen, and do not stretch it too tightly except to keep the wound alone.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it be thus for one day or two days, until the abscess is appeased, then loosen it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer gradually medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and be sure that the wound is gradually clean, and do not leave any ointment, nor allow it to assemble with flesh, for when flesh assembles above the skin of the brain, they corrupt and perish, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the sacrum, it kills above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed if any bad accidents befall the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if nothing worse comes except through the medicine that has been put on, which has such virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one cloth, and place it on the sacrum;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then perform the cure by means of cures that are necessary, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only becomes bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, so it is necessary that you make your little nail or perforation in the neck, and place equal that break within your nail index, and at the pocket by fleeing, until the neck returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the neck, and cannot come back into place, so it is necessary that you put it equal to the head of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, so do it again, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is cooled down, then put a cloth of linen on the head of the neck, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put another of the other part, if there is a break there; and let the tents be so big that they fill the perforations of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And certain restorers say that one should moisten the tents with butter and change each day. It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the concoction of hen's egg white, and miller's powder; then leave the tent, until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts a goose's neck in place of tents, and if it has a soft cloth around it, and the break is held, and blows on the patient between; then do as you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear on the neck while you are working there, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a small quantity of aquilina.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not appear there, put an emplaster away from it, made of spelt flour and incense powder, mixed with hen's egg white, then place light poultices on top, and do not bind the neck.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break of the neck is small and it is broken into little pieces, then draw it out with suitable instruments for that, then close the cut, and care for things as they grow together in flesh, and soldering, just as with emplasters and ointments suitable for that.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the neck, then care for tents and put poultices of wool, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw's dislocation
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, and there is no wound outside, and the break is outside only so far as to be felt internally, but is not broken in two, except that it is swollen inside, then one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right side, that you put your little finger index in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jaw, then put your little finger index of the right hand, and gently push the break inside, and adjust it with the other hand away from it, and make equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is dislocated in two parts, so it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of teeth occurs, or dislocation, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw cerate, and put on one double cloth; and put on the cloth a great piece well made, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then release it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put an emplaster on, made of miller's powder with hen's egg white or spelt flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put a light linen cloth on top, and if the emplasters dry up, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it so until he is healed; many times he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, then return none of the bone that has been removed; but subtlety in removing with suitable instruments for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it by degrees according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then close the wound, if it is wide, and put on one or more suitable emplasters to bring about flesh growth, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks in several places before the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners: or it is broken and dislocated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or it has a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the break has no wound, that you have two attendants, one of whom holds the shoulder piece that feels the fractured forcele; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break equal to your fingers, so that the form be as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then put under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth or linen, and make it as thick as your necessity demands; and stretch and lift the forcele, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you place the break equal, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcele away from the outside, because it comes from deep down, then it is necessary that the patient lies comfortably on his bedstead, and put a middle pillow under the shoulder; and have the attendants lower the shoulder so that the bone of the forcele is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your fingers, and if you find it debrisied, so it is necessary that you split it open; and draw forth the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join by any means, then cut off at one of the incisors you have; but put this instrument under the forcele, to ward off the syphilitic.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and appears like a spoon, and is not rough, and be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one be wide and the other be narrow, just like the dislocation of the wound that you made when you cut into the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, if it is to be cut, and the ulceration is small, or you doubt whether it is a hot abscess, if you employ the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a cold abscess comes, then moisten it with cloths in oil of rose, and aloe, and wine, and put on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone a plaster made from mill powder and egg white, and put on light poultices above, and put a spear under the splint, if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide band of palm, then put one cloth double over the poultices and plaster; then take a fine roll three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that band, so that the top of the band is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the roll on the gash, and turn the band around the collarbone, and under the splint of the well person, and under the splint of the sick person; and rewrap each part, and when you see that the band holds the gash in good condition, and you see clearly that the roll is not moving on the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the band loosens, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the sick person sit on his back, and put a small pillow under the splint, so that he can lift the aid in high; thus alleviate the breakage of the collarbone by aligning the shoulder, or bind the arm to the neck, and do not release it unless bad accidents come, until 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the plaster if you see that it is needed, and tighten it and leave it thus, until he is restored; and she is restored in about 28 days, and to some people less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or becomes wide and does not fit well; nor is it swollen except by touch; then arrange according to the figure of the break, and rewrap according to its natural form in all ways you can; then put on the skin powder made from mill dust with egg white, and light poultices, and put a double cloth on top; then put on a wide and fine roll, a little larger than the shoulder, and if there is a swelling anywhere on the shoulder below the roll, use that swelling to apply linen bandages so that the roll remains even; and then bind it all with a strong band tightly, so that the roll does not move from its place, and check the band each day; and every time it becomes swollen, bind it again, and put the roll back in its place if it has moved from its place, and make the patient sit on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be careful, for it is not the bone that becomes loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points below the key, then do this, and the bone, and do what we have said in the break of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the rib break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The ribs are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break at the back. And when it is broken in the middle, it descends below and the patient feels great pain, and lacks breath, and all around, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the swelling on the broken bone, and one feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient sits on their back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and gently puts it even in all ways you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put on plasters and poultices above the fine roll of salt, or other light stuff, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the band around again at the back, and bind it well, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it becomes swollen, then bind it again; and if it needs to be released because of corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and release it, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come forth with regards to cures; then rewrap the plaster, and bind it until they are healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib break
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakage of the ribs does not come from anything other than large blows after the back, and from the top inside, and do not bend except because they are swollen; and one feels well in the investigation at the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the breakage even, as it should be. And then put on a plaster, and bind with a roll, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the fabric; and breathes with difficulty, and all around, and vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a grievous sickness, and the ancients have put great wit into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly to push back the breakage forward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless hot abscesses come, if they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let him be healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that you put poultices on the place to draw forth strongly, and it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the poultice will attract the superfluities to the place due to the weakness of the flesh.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the place with moist linen in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to put even the bandage around, then be careful about the treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone which pierces the fabric, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to open up on the broken rib, and put below a tool to ward off the shrapnel; and then one must cut the bone, and pull it lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and cure with plasters until he is healed. And if hot abscesses come, then put on moist cloths in rose oil, and put on the place; and cure meanwhile the place as it needs for abscess, and be careful to sit above the back where it should, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes that breaks at the bone of the neck, and then it bends; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if he moves them and feels well when one strains and pricks them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and the patient will be cured if one puts care into it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it will recover or not, if take heed if his feet are softened, and if the accident is in his hands and on his back there is windiness and emission without volition; and when one has soothed him on his belly, then there is emission without volition. And when he is soothed on his back and he wants to be eased, he cannot. Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is more easy.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you rub if there is a warm abscess, then put oil of rose or oil of egg yolk on the spine until it is calmed; then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is dislocated, you should cover it with the key; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, then apply an ointment releasing fat, until he is cured; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the jaw", take your pouch from your left hand and put it even with your right hand as far as you can, then apply the poultice and bandage on it, if needed; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do so, and remove them, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does, then there is a slight diminution at the head; and it swells along, and declines in the pelvis, and comes to the patient's pain at the location, and pricks, and inflames what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand on top, as far as you are above the breakage; and know what kind of breakage it is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, then put equal pressure on that breakage, until it returns to its natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is of the long bone, or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of that breakage becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, then put on a poultice, then put on a bandage of wood or key, and restrain the breakage, so that it does not move; and bind the location below the ribs, until the limbs are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if warm abscesses come, do not touch them, until the warm abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as needed, if there is no bad accident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is what is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one piece of wood smooth and full of growth, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with two bands, and stretch them up high, and make the patient sit on one chair; then throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it comes to the level, and has about a half a curve of wood, then stretch onto some heavy thing or have the assistants extend downwards; then put the mirror under the breakage equal to their hands together, until the breakage returns as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one soothes the patient on his hayre, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants to have one hold what is on the breakage with their hands, and the others hold below each band, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then bind one band below the breakage and on top of the breakage, and have each assistant stretch to their part. And if the breakage is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one band midway under the armpit, and another towards the arm, under the breakage; and also if the breakage is towards the arm, it is necessary to put one light band, without labor, until the breakage is even on the top and on the arm; then make the breakage equal as needed, and bind it, if warm abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if warm abscesses come, do not bind it at all until seven days, and put on a damp linen cloth in oil and rosewater, until the warm abscess is calmed; then bind it, and the manner of binding is that you put the poultice on the breakage, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and apply the compress, and bind on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a position to be straightened without being hindered by anything, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use strait bands, and put on the breakage a band wider and stronger than the others, with two or three fingerbreadths between each band, and have each band so large that it passes over the breakage three fingers from each side; then bind on the bands, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, stronger and less strait.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the sores and stiffness, as we have said, in the healing of the broken member, and you doubt the warm abscess, then leave it alone until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each band every three days to see that there is no itching or swelling that comes to the limb, or that numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tight. If so, address it as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	Et si nulz telz accidens ni vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", where one is small and is the one that supports the pouch; and the other is large, and is the one that is below, towards the little thumb; by chance, it breaks the large foscile alone, or the small, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are both broken together. If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then you must gently extend it a little and make equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bones, then you must strain more strongly; and extend it on one cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little thumbs lower than the other thumbs, and have the patient cross over himself, with a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch the assistant's arm to the part below his hand, or to one of its joints, and another assistant above. And then set it equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then set each one in its place, and if any are loose that can be pulled out, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a new one and use the bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if you have spoken of the break with a wound in a singular chapter, then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses that arise, then take a cloth made of wax made from oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and wrap the cloth subtly over the abscesses, until they are calmed. And then remove the wax, and put an ointment made with flour of the mill mixed with egg whites on it; and set the splints, and let the splint of the break be a little stronger and a bit wider than the others; and know that it should have 7 splints or more in different dispositions: whether the break is in one bone or two; and strain more over the break than any other part, and always less as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths be above the break soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread, from which it is strained, be made of linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accidents happen to the member, such as pruritus that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member in warm water, until those prurites are calmed; and let the member rest not too tightly. And then resume the straining, and if the joint is softened and the bones loosened, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the stiffness cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and let it be like that for some days, until the stiffness goes away, and then strain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said come to the patient, then do not remove the bandage until 20 days or so, and then let the hands be at his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and gesture, and sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in 30 days or 35 days, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and as to the thumbs, there are many breakings, and it does not come but that pleasure comes many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit directly in front of him evenly; then put his hand on the stretched cloth, and stretch out the assistants to the broken bones, and set them equal with the mirror, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and poultices, if abscesses do not come, then place a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a cloth made of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the edge of the palm around the belly of the hand, then make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken hand; and then strain with a long cloth, and let the splint be as soft as the palm of the hand, and strain, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the far end, then it is necessary that you put a splint on top and another one below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the joint between the thumbs.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our thumbs, such as the index or one of the others, then set it straight and equal, as it is necessary; and strain with the palm, and if you see that you put a small straight splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is at the other thumb, then set it straight and equal, and tie it with the healthy thumb that comes after; or you tie them all together in one holding, as it seems best, or you put a splint on top, such as the pouchet; and take care of the restoration and the disposition of the hot abscess, and attend to what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken toe
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the toe is many times broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one thread is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches each assistant's thread to its equal part; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near to the root of the toe, then one of the threads should be towards the little finger, and the other threads below the break. And also if it is near to the ankle, and then it should be the thread beneath the ankle, and the extension downwards; then set the mirror so that the bone is equal to its two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and tie it, if hot abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it be calmed first and then return to your work and care; the binding is done in the same manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It covient that thou envelops upon the binding .i. bandages doubled in two or three, and removest the superfluities, then turn thy leg so that the heels come to the root of the knee, and put one long thread between the crotch and the leg, below the knee, and let the chief of the thread come above; then turn upon the leg and upon the crotch the bandage, then set upon the binding stays, and set one stay upon the bone of the leg; then take hold the space eight days between the leg and the crotch with soft cloths to make equal the straining, then begin to bind strongly three or four turns upon the binding; and when thou goest further up on the binding, and less the straining; then hearken to the two heels of the thread that thou hast put between the leg and the crotch, and bind three stays that are above, then return below to the chief of the thread, until thou comest below the foot; and the straining, if it doth not move from its place, then leave it thus, lest it come aposteme or inflammation or any such thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, then loosen it, and adjust what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pinch, then it is necessary to remove them if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the flesh and draw out the force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And once the crotch is broken like this, one puts stays in it, as in an aid and on the arm; however, in this restoration made, the patient does not ache.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the crotch is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversities of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
